Conditional Mahr: Conditions on Residence or Polygyny
Rulings on mahr conditioned on acts or abstentions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three scenarios of conditional mahr, explain the Hanafi positions, and apply the rule to derive the dower when the condition is breached.

Core Idea
A beneficial condition for the wife is valid; an alternative dower based on a future event creates uncertainty, triggering mahr al-mithl within the named bounds.

In Hanafi law, the wife may stipulate conditions in the marriage contract that benefit her, such as not being moved from her residence or not having a co-wife. These conditions are valid and, if fulfilled, the full named dower is due. However, if the dower itself is made conditional on an uncertain event, the dower becomes unknown and must be replaced by mahr al-mithl, though the text limits this to the named amounts. This lesson unpacks the third scenario and the disagreement among the imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditional mahr scenarios
The passage presents three cases: (1) condition not to take her out of the village, (2) condition not to marry another woman, (3) dower of 1,000 if he stays but 2,000 if he takes her out. Note which are agreed upon and which are disputed.
The first two are undisputed among Hanafi imams.
2
Understand the Hanafi ruling for the first two scenarios
If the husband fulfills the condition, she gets the named dower (1,000). If he breaches, the condition is broken, and the dower remains as agreed? Actually, the text does not discuss breach of these conditions; it only says if he fulfills, she gets it. But the implication is that if he breaches, the condition is void but the marriage and dower remain valid. Focus on the agreement.
3
Analyze the third scenario: alternative dower
Here the dower is conditional on staying (1,000) or leaving (2,000). This creates uncertainty because the actual amount is unknown until the event. The passage records four positions: Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf & Muhammad), Zufar, and al-Shafi'i.
4
Compare the four positions on the third scenario
Abu Hanifa: mahr al-mithl between 1,000 and 2,000. Sahibayn: both conditions valid, so she gets the amount corresponding to the actual event. Zufar: conditions invalid, so mahr al-mithl without bounds. Shafi'i: mahr al-mithl in all cases. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
Sahibayn analogize to sewing a garment for two different known rates.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa: the dower is uncertain, so mahr al-mithl is due, but limited by the two named amounts.
This is the Hanafi school's authoritative view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو على أن لا يخرجها أو على أن لا يتزوج عليها، أو على ألف إن أقام بها، من المدنية أي درهم مهراً أي بالبصرة مثلاً أن لا عينيه، ووجه الاستحسان أن حقه عند الطلاق سلامة نصف المقبوض من جهتها وقد وصل إليه، ولا يبالي باختلاف السبب عند حصول المقصود. (مستخلص) الألف: أي المهر المسمى وأبرأته من جميع المهر. (ط) ووهبت الألف يعني جميع المهر المقبوض وغير المقبوض. (ع) عرض: إن تزوجها على عرض معين ثم وهبته له. (ع) : قبل القبض وكذا لو وهبت نصف العرض وهو خلاف النقد كالثوب والحيوان. (ط) لم يرجع عليها بشيء [جواب المسائل الثلاثة الحصول المقصود. (ط، ع)] أما في المسألة الأولى فلأنه سلم له عين ما يستحقه بالطلاق قبل الدخول فلا يستوجب عليها شيئاً آخر غايته أن هذه السلامة حصلت بسبب الهبة لا بالطلاق، ولا يبالي باختلاف السبب عند سلامة المقصود، وكذا في المسألة الثانية لو قبضت خمس مائة ثم وهبت الألف كله المقبوض وغيره، أو وهبت الباقي في ذمة الزوج ثم طلقها قبل الدخول لم يرجع عليها بشيء أيضاً؛ إذ وصل إليه عين ما يستحقه كما مر وكذا في الصورة الثالثة لو تزوجها على ما يتعين بالتعيين كالعرض فوهبت له نصفه أو كله قبضته أو لا ثم طلقها قبل الدخول لم يرجع عليها بشيء؛ لأن حقه سلامة نصف المقبوض بلا عوض من جهتها بالطلاق قبل الدخول وقد وصل إليه؛ لأنه مما يتعين فكان الموهوب عين المهر فسلم له مقصوده فلا يرجع بشيء إلا أن عدم الرجوع في مسألة العرض مقيد بما إذا لم يتعيب عندها. (فتح) هذه الثانية من أو على أن لا يتزوج ثلاث مسائل: الأولى منها ما مر من أنه تزوجها على ألف على أن لا يخرجها من هذه القرية أي شرط ما فيه منفعة لها أو لأبيها أو لذي رحم محرم منها مما يحل الانتفاع به، والثانية: أنه تزوجها على ألف على أن لا يتزوج عليها بامرأة أخرى ففي هاتين المسألتين إن وفى الزوج بالشرط فلها الألف ولا خلاف بين أئمتنا فيها؛ لأن الألف صلح مهراً وقد تم رضاها به والثالثة: أنه تزوجها على ألف على شرط إن أقام بها في هذه القرية، وعلى ألفين إن أخرجها منها. أنه سمي لها مهراً على تقدير، ومهراً على تقدير آخر، ففي هذه الصورة اختلاف في الوفاء بالشرط وعدم الوفاء به، فعند أبي حنيفة: إن أخرجها من البصرة فلها مهر المثل لا يزاد على الألفين ولا ينقص عن الألف، وقالا: الشرطان جميعاً جائزان فلها الألف إن أقام بها، والألفان عند خروجها منها؛ لأنهما عقدان ببدلين معلومين فأشبه خياطة الثوب رومياً أو فارسياً، وقال زفر الشرطان فاسدان؛ لأنه ذكر للبضع بدلين على سبيل البدل لا على سبيل الاجتماع، فيكون مجهولاً فيفسد، فيكون لها مهر المثل، وعند الشافعي: يجب مهر مثلها في الحالين
Or on condition that he does not take her out, or that he does not marry another woman, or for one thousand if he stays with her, from the city—meaning dirham as dower—in Basra, for example... The gist: And the third issue: he marries her for one thousand on condition that if he stays in this village [she gets one thousand], and two thousand if he takes her out. He named for her a dower on one condition and a dower on another condition. In this image there is disagreement regarding fulfillment of the condition or not. According to Abu Hanifa: if he takes her out of Basra, she gets mahr al-mithl, not exceeding two thousand nor less than one thousand. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: both conditions are valid, so she gets one thousand if he stays, and two thousand if he takes her out, because they are two contracts with two known compensations, resembling the sewing of a garment as Roman or Persian. Zufar said both conditions are invalid because he mentioned two compensations for the vulva on an alternative basis, not cumulative, so it is unknown, thus invalid, so she gets mahr al-mithl. According to al-Shafi'i: she gets her mahr al-mithl in both cases.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage addresses three images of conditional mahr. The first two images are straightforward: (1) husband conditions that he will not take her out of the village, and (2) conditions that he will not marry another woman. If he fulfills the condition, the wife gets the specified dower (one thousand). There is no disagreement among the Hanafi imams on these two; the condition is beneficial to the wife and thus valid.

The third image is more complex: the dower is specified as one thousand if he stays in the village, but two thousand if he takes her out. Abu Hanifa rules that if he actually takes her out, she gets mahr al-mithl, but capped between the two amounts (not more than two thousand, not less than one thousand). This is because the dower is uncertain; the condition is alternative and not cumulative, so the contract is valid but the dower is determined by mahr al-mithl with those bounds. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) say both conditions are valid as if they are separate contracts; she gets one thousand if he stays, two thousand if he leaves. They analogize to hiring a tailor for Roman or Persian stitching—two known rates. Zufar says both conditions are invalid because the dower is unknown (it depends on future event), so the contract is valid but she gets mahr al-mithl unconditionally. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that mahr al-mithl applies in both scenarios.

Thus, this is both an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn vs Zufar) and inter-madhhab (Hanafi vs Shafi'i). The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa: the dower in the third image is mahr al-mithl within the specified bounds.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): Condition stipulated in the marriage contract, here benefiting the wife.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): Proper dower of a woman's peers, used when the specified dower is invalid or uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling in the third scenario (dower of 1,000 if he stays, 2,000 if he leaves) when the husband actually takes her out?
A) She gets 1,000.
B) She gets 2,000.
C) She gets mahr al-mithl, not less than 1,000 nor more than 2,000.
D) The marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
An alternative dower based on a future event leads to uncertainty, triggering mahr al-mithl bounded by the named amounts in Abu Hanifa's relied-upon view.

Wife's Gift of Mahr Before Consummation: No Return After Divorce
Ruling and istihsan proof for no return of gifted mahr after divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife gifts back the mahr and is divorced before consummation, and explain the istihsan proof.

Core Idea
If a wife gifts the mahr to her husband, his right to half upon pre-consummation divorce is already fulfilled—means don't matter.

In Hanafi law, when a husband divorces his wife before consummation, he is normally entitled to half the mahr. But what if the wife has already given that half back as a gift? This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies that the husband does not get anything back, because his right to the half has already been satisfied. The proof is istihsan (juristic preference): the objective—the husband receiving half the mahr safely—is achieved, regardless of whether it came through the divorce or through her gift.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a wife gifting back the mahr (or part of it) to her husband—either before or after receiving it—followed by divorce before consummation. The ruling: the husband does not reclaim anything.
The ruling applies to three scenarios: (1) she gifts half after receiving it, (2) she gifts the entire mahr (received and unreceived), (3) she gifts a specific item that was the mahr.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites istihsan as the proof, not qiyas. The istihsan reasoning is: the husband's right at divorce is to have half of the received mahr safely come to him from the wife's side.
The dalil is aqli (reasoning-based) rather than naqli (textual).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is attainment of the objective—safety of the half. The means (gift vs. divorce) does not matter because the objective is met. Thus, the husband cannot reclaim.
This is an example of istihsan overriding a default qiyas that might require return.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage does not detail disagreement, but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi. Other schools may hold that the gift is a return of mahr and the husband can still claim half, but this text focuses on the Hanafi view.
Cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الألف أو قبضت النصف ووهبت الألف أو ما بقي أو وهبت عرض المهر قبل المرأة من أي نصف ألف المهر باقي المهر وهو خمس مائة درهم القبض أو بعده فطلقت قبل الوطء لم يرجع عليها بشيء، ولو نكحها بألف على أن لا يخرجها أو على أن لا يتزوج عليها، أو على ألف إن أقام بها، من المدنية بامرأة أخرى أي درهم أي المرأة درهم مهراً أي بالبصرة مثلاً أن لا عينيه، ووجه الاستحسان أن حقه عند الطلاق سلامة نصف المقبوض من جهتها وقد وصل إليه، ولا يبالي باختلاف السبب عند حصول المقصود. (مستخلص) الألف: أي المهر المسمى وأبرأته من جميع المهر. (ط) ووهبت الألف يعني جميع المهر المقبوض وغير المقبوض. (ع) عرض: إن تزوجها على عرض معين ثم وهبته له. (ع) : قبل القبض وكذا لو وهبت نصف العرض وهو خلاف النقد كالثوب والحيوان. (ط) لم يرجع عليها بشيء [جواب المسائل الثلاثة الحصول المقصود. (ط، ع)] أما في المسألة الأولى فلأنه سلم له عين ما يستحقه بالطلاق قبل الدخول فلا يستوجب عليها شيئاً آخر غايته أن هذه السلامة حصلت بسبب الهبة لا بالطلاق، ولا يبالي باختلاف السبب عند سلامة المقصود، وكذا في المسألة الثانية لو قبضت خمس مائة ثم وهبت الألف كله المقبوض وغيره، أو وهبت الباقي في ذمة الزوج ثم طلقها قبل الدخول لم يرجع عليها بشيء أيضاً؛ إذ وصل إليه عين ما يستحقه كما مر وكذا في الصورة الثالثة لو تزوجها على ما يتعين بالتعيين كالعرض فوهبت له نصفه أو كله قبضته أو لا ثم طلقها قبل الدخول لم يرجع عليها بشيء؛ لأن حقه سلامة نصف المقبوض بلا عوض من جهتها بالطلاق قبل الدخول وقد وصل إليه؛ لأنه مما يتعين فكان الموهوب عين المهر فسلم له مقصوده فلا يرجع بشيء إلا أن عدم الرجوع في مسألة العرض مقيد بما إذا لم يتعيب عندها. (فتح)
The thousand or she received half and gifted the thousand or what remained or she gifted a specific dower before the woman from any half of the thousand dower the remaining dower which is five hundred dirhams before receipt or after, then he divorced before intercourse, he does not take back anything from her. The basis of istihsan is that his right at divorce is the safety of half of the received [dower] from her side, and it has reached him, and one does not care about the difference of means when the objective is attained. ... (Commentary explains the three cases: gifting half, gifting all, gifting a specific item.)
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its explanatory commentary. The core ruling: if a wife gifts back the dower (or part of it) to the husband—whether she had received it or not—and then the husband divorces her before consummation, he does not get anything back. The proof is istihsan (juristic preference): the husband's right upon divorce is to have half of the received dower safely come to him from the wife's side. This safety is achieved through her gift, so the means (gift vs. divorce) does not matter. The commentary elaborates three cases: (1) she gifts half after receiving it, (2) she gifts the entire thousand (received and unreceived), and (3) she gifts a specific item (e.g., cloth) that becomes the dower. In all, the husband gets nothing because his right is fulfilled. Exception: for a specific item, if it became defective with her, the ruling may differ.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife as an obligatory part of the marriage contract.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from a clear analogy for a stronger reason.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession or receipt of the mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, if a wife gifts the entire unmilled mahr (1000 dirhams) to her husband before receiving any of it, and then he divorces her before consummation, what is the ruling?
A) The husband must pay her 500 dirhams.
B) The husband does not get anything back.
C) The husband takes back 500 dirhams.
D) The husband takes back the full 1000 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
When a wife gifts back the mahr, the husband's right to half upon pre-consummation divorce is already satisfied, so he cannot reclaim anything—the means (gift vs. divorce) does not matter as long as the objective of safety of half is achieved.

Conditional Mahr: Three Cases and Madhhab Disputes
Inter-madhhab dispute on conditional mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on conditional mahr and evaluate the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, Zufar, and other schools.

Core Idea
When mahr depends on a future event, Abu Hanifa protects the wife's consent with mahr al-mithl, capped by the named amounts.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute about a marriage contract where the dower amount is conditional on whether the husband stays in or leaves the town. The Hanafi school itself has internal disagreement (Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn vs Zufar), and other schools weigh in. Understanding the different positions and their underlying proofs sharpens your ability to analyze contractual conditions in nikah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Cases
The passage recalls two earlier cases (condition not to take wife out of town; condition not to marry another woman) and introduces the third: mahr set at 1000 if he stays, 2000 if he leaves. Distinguish these three scenarios.
The first two cases have no dispute when the condition is fulfilled; the third triggers ikhtilaf.
2
State the Hanafi Positions
Write the rulings of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf & Muhammad), and Zufar clearly. Note the key difference: Abu Hanifa uses mahr al-mithl with caps; the Sahibayn enforce both conditions as valid; Zufar voids both conditions.
The Sahibayn analogize to tailoring a garment with two price options.
3
Analyze the Proofs
Examine the reasoning: Abu Hanifa says the second condition involves risk (gharar), so the wife's consent to the lower amount is negated when that condition is breached. The Sahibayn see two known alternatives, thus valid. Zufar sees disjunctive uncertainty.
The hadith about fulfilling conditions is invoked by opponents but rebutted.
4
Compare to Other Schools
Shafi'i always gives mahr al-mithl; Malik invalidates the marriage; Hanbalis annul if condition unfulfilled. Note their proofs and the Hanafi response.
The Hanafi response argues that the hadith does not support annulment.
5
Derive the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, if the husband breaches the condition (e.g., leaves town), the wife gets mahr al-mithl (between 1000 and 2000). Under the Sahibayn, she gets the higher named amount (2000). Under Shafi'i, always mahr al-mithl. Under Malik, no marriage.
This difference directly affects the wife's financial entitlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذه الثانية من أو على أن لا يتزوج ثلاث مسائل: الأولى منها ما مر من أنه تزوجها على ألف على أن لا يخرجها من هذه القرية أي شرط ما فيه منفعة لها أو لأبيها أو لذي رحم محرم منها مما يحل الانتفاع به، والثانية: أنه تزوجها على ألف على أن لا يتزوج عليها بامرأة أخرى ففي هاتين المسألتين إن وفى الزوج بالشرط فلها الألف ولا خلاف بين أئمتنا فيها؛ لأن الألف صلح مهراً وقد تم رضاها به والثالثة: أنه تزوجها على ألف على شرط إن أقام بها في هذه القرية، وعلى ألفين إن أخرجها منها. والحاصل: مهراً على تقدير، ومهراً على تقدير آخر، ففي هذه الصورة اختلاف في الوفاء بالشرط وعدم الوفاء به، فعند أبي حنيفة: إن أخرجها من البصرة فلها مهر المثل لا يزاد على الألفين ولا ينقص عن الألف، وقالا: الشرطان جميعاً جائزان فلها الألف إن أقام بها، والألفان عند خروجها منها؛ لأنهما عقدان ببدلين معلومين فأشبه خياطة الثوب رومياً أو فارسياً، وقال زفر الشرطان فاسدان؛ لأنه ذكر للبضع بدلين على سبيل البدل لا على سبيل الاجتماع، فيكون مجهولاً فيفسد، فيكون لها مهر المثل، وعند الشافعي: يجب مهر مثلها في الحالين، وعند مالك: يفسد النكاح في الحالين وعند أبي حنيفة: الشرط الأول صحيح لا خطر فيه، والثاني فيه خطر فيجب مهر المثل؛ لأنه سمي ما لها فيه نفع، فعند فواته ينعدم رضاها بالألف، وقالت الحنابلة: إن لم يف بالشرط يفسخ النكاح؛ لقوله عليه: "أحق الشروط أن توفوا ما استحللتم به من الفروج، ولنا قوله عليه: "كل شرط ليس في كتاب الله فهو باطل، وليس فيه هذه الشروط ، ولا دليل في الحديث على مدعاهم؛ لأنه عليها جعله أحق بالإيفاء فمن أين لهم الفسخ عند فواته. (عيني، فتح، مستخلص) وفى به أي وفى الزوج بالشرط في المسألة الأولى بأن لم يخرجها عن البلدة وفي الثانية بأن لم يتزوج عليها. (ع) في الصور جميعاً؛ لأنه هو المسمى وقد تم رضاها به (ع) وإلا : أي وإن لم يوف بالشرط بأن أخرجها من البلدة، أو تزوج عليها، أو لم يقم بها بالبصرة. رمز الحقائق: ۲۱۳/۱] فمهر المثل: أي فالواجب لها عليه مهر مثلها لا يزاد على ألفين في الصورة الثالثة؛ لأنها رضيت بهما ولا ينقص عن ا الألف؛ لأنه رضي به. (ع)
This second [section] from 'or on condition that he not marry another woman' has three cases: ... The summary: a dower on one estimate and a dower on another. In this case there is disagreement on fulfillment of the condition. According to Abu Hanifa: if he takes her out of Basra, she gets mahr al-mithl, not exceeding two thousand nor less than one thousand. The Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: both conditions are valid, so she gets one thousand if he stays, and two thousand if he takes her out, because they are two contracts with known alternatives, similar to tailoring a garment Roman or Persian. Zufar said both conditions are corrupt because he mentioned two alternatives disjunctively, making it unknown, so she gets mahr al-mithl. Al-Shafi'i: mahr al-mithl in both cases. Malik: the marriage is corrupt in both cases. The Hanabila: if he does not fulfill the condition, the marriage is annulled. Our response: there is no basis for annulment. (Commentary follows).
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning a marriage where the dower is conditioned on an event (e.g., staying in a town gives 1000, leaving gives 2000). The Hanafi school's position: Abu Hanifa rules that if the condition is breached (e.g., he takes her out), the wife gets mahr al-mithl, capped at the higher named amount and floored at the lower. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) treat both conditions as valid binding options, like two separate contracts. Zufar says both conditions are invalid, leading to mahr al-mithl. Shafi'i and Malik give mahr al-mithl or annul marriage respectively. Hanabila call for annulment. The passage defends Abu Hanifa's view: the first condition (not taking her out) is valid; the second is risky because it involves a future event, so mahr al-mithl applies to protect her consent.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to that of women similar to the bride in status, used when the named dower is invalid or unknown.
شرط (shart): Condition; a stipulation in a contract that may affect the rights of parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man marries a woman on the condition that he stays in the town (1000 dower) or leaves it (2000 dower), and he does leave, what does the wife get?
A) Exactly 2000.
B) Exactly 1000.
C) Mahr al-mithl not exceeding 2000 and not less than 1000.
D) Mahr al-mithl without any cap.

Key Takeaway
In conditional mahr, Abu Hanifa's view balances the wife's consent with the named amounts, making it the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Determining Mahr When Dower is One of Two Items or Unspecified
Ruling on mahr when dower is one of two specified items or an unspecified animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a dower is named as one of two specific items or an unspecified animal, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl is the baseline; the named items only adjust it by mutual consent.

In marriage contracts, the dower (mahr) is a fundamental obligation. Sometimes the dower is ambiguously stated—such as 'this slave or that slave'—or left unspecified as to type (e.g., 'a horse or a donkey' without details). The Hanafi school has a detailed methodology to determine the mahr in these cases, with a notable internal dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers (a) dower stated as one of two specific items, and (b) dower stated as an unspecified animal (or type). Note the difference in the level of ambiguity.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's position
They hold that when the dower is one of two items, the wife gets the lesser value because it is certain. For an unspecified animal, gross ignorance invalidates the naming, so mahr al-mithl applies.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's position
He first imposes mahr al-mithl as the hakam, then compares it to the named values: she gets whichever aligns with her consent (higher if mahr al-mithl > both, lower if < both, and if equal she chooses). For an unspecified animal, same as Sahibayn because of jahl fahish.
4
Apply the rule to examples
Practice with numeric values to see the practical difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa the wife may receive more than the lesser named item; under the Sahibayn she always gets the lesser. The Shafi'i school also holds mahr al-mithl in all ambiguous cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نكحها على هذا العبد أو على هذا العبد حكم مهر المثل، وعلى فرس أو حمار الألف مهر الأرفع قيمة، وعند مالك: يفسد النكاح في الحالين وعند أبي حنيفة: الشرط الأول صحيح لا خطر فيه، والثاني فيه خطر فيجب مهر المثل؛ لأنه سمي ما لها فيه نفع، فعند فواته ينعدم رضاها بالألف، وقالت الحنابلة: إن لم يف بالشرط يفسخ النكاح؛ لقوله عليه: "أحق الشروط أن توفوا ما استحللتم به من الفروج، ولنا قوله عليه: "كل شرط ليس في كتاب الله فهو باطل، وليس فيه هذه الشروط ، ولا دليل في الحديث على مدعاهم؛ لأنه عليها جعله أحق بالإيفاء فمن أين لهم الفسخ عند فواته. (ع)] أي إذا تزوجها على هذا العبد أو على ذلك وقيمتهما متفاوتة كان المهر حَكَماً، فإن كان مهر المثل أرفع من أرفعهما فلها الأرفع منهما؛ لثبوت رضائها به، وإن كان أوكس من أو كسهما فلها الأوكس؛ لثبوت رضاء الزوج به ، وإن كانت قيمتهما متساوية فينبغي أن يكون المهر أحدهما على اختيار المرأة تأخذ أياً شاءت وتحكيم مهر المثل في صورة التفاوت عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: لها الأوكس على كل حال لهما أن المصير إلى مهر المثل لتعذر إيجاب المسمى ولا تعذر ههنا؛ لأن الأقل ثابت بيقين، ولأبي حنيفة: أن مهر المثل هو الواجب الأصلي بدليل أنه يجب بنفس العقد من غير تسميته، ولا ينقص عن الأدنى؛ لوجود رضا الزوج به وكذا لا يزيد على الأعلى؛ لوجود رضاها به رمز الحقائق: ۲۱۳/۱] (مستخلص) وعلى فرس أو حمار أي لو تزوجها على فرس فقط أو تزوج على حمار فقط يعني تزوج على حيوان ذكر جنسه دون نوعه فإنه مخير بين أن يسلم فرساً وسطاً وبين أن يسلم إليها قيمة الفرس الوسط، وليس المعنى أنه تزوجها على هذا أو هذا على معنى الشك والترديد، بل كلمة "أو " ههنا للتنويع، ولو تزوجها على فرس أو حمار بمعنى الشك والتردد بينهما، فالجواب فيه كالجواب في المسألة الأولى من تحكيم مهر المثل عنده، ووجوب الأقل عندهما، ولو تزوجها على حيوان ولم يبين جنسه بأن تزوجها على دابة بطلت التسمية، ويجب مهر المثل؛ لتفاحش الجهالة، وقال الشافعي: يجب مهر المثل في الوجهين جميعاً. رمز الحقائق: ٢١٤/١] لأن عنده ما لا يصلح ثمنا في البيع لا يصلح مسمى في النكاح؛ إذ كل واحد منهما عقد معاوضة، ولنا أنه معاوضة مال بغير مال فجعلناه بمنزلة التزام المال
If he marries her on this slave or that slave, the ruling is mahr al-mithl; and on a horse or a donkey, the mahr is the one of highest value. ... (Commentary explains the dispute: Abu Hanifa says mahr al-mithl, the Two say the lesser value; if the dower is an unspecified animal, the naming is invalid and mahr al-mithl is due because of gross ignorance.)
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: (1) When the dower is stated as one of two specific items (e.g., this slave or that), Abu Hanifa says the wife gets mahr al-mithl, which then is compared to the values: if mahr al-mithl is higher than both, she gets the higher of the two named items; if lower than both, she gets the lower; if equal, she chooses. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say she always gets the lesser of the two because the lesser is certain. (2) When the dower is an unspecified animal (like a horse or donkey without specifics), the naming is invalid due to gross ignorance (jahl fāḥish), so mahr al-mithl is due. The Shafi'i school requires mahr al-mithl in both cases because they consider only items that can serve as prices in a sale valid as dower. The Hanafi response: marriage is a exchange of property for non-property (the wife's mithl), so the rules differ from sale.

Key Terms
الجهالة الفاحشة (al-jahalah al-fāhishah): Gross ignorance or ambiguity that invalidates the dower naming, e.g., not specifying the type of animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man marries a woman on the dower of 'this slave or that' (one valuable, one cheap), what does she get?
A) The cheaper slave (the lesser value).
B) The more expensive slave (the higher value).
C) She chooses either.
D) Mahr al-mithl, and then compared to the values: if mahr al-mithl is higher, she gets the higher slave; if lower, she gets the lower.

Key Takeaway
When the dower is ambiguous, Abu Hanifa uses mahr al-mithl as the benchmark and then adjusts based on the named values, while the Sahibayn insist on the lesser certain amount.

Mahr Specified by Genus Only: The Medium Standard
Ruling on mahr specified by genus only

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when mahr is specified by genus only and explain that the husband gives a medium specimen or its value.

Core Idea
When mahr is specified by genus, the husband may give a medium or its value – the marriage is valid.

In this lesson, we examine a case from Al-Hidayah where the mahr is defined only by its genus — 'a horse' or 'a donkey' without specifying the type. Marghinani clarifies that this specification is valid and the husband has the option to deliver a medium-quality animal or its cash value. We also explore the meaning of the word 'or' in this context and the intra-Hanafi disagreement when 'or' indicates doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the nikah contract where the mahr is specified by genus only (e.g., 'a horse' or 'a donkey' without type). The ruling is that the specification is valid (sahih) and the husband must give a medium-quality animal or its value.
Medium (wasat) means average, neither the best nor the worst.
2
Understand the wasat standard
The Hanafi standard for unspecified type is 'wasat' (medium). This balances the rights of both parties – the wife receives a fair amount, and the husband is not forced to give the best.
If the husband chooses to give value, it must be the value of a medium specimen.
3
Distinguish 'or' for diversification vs. doubt
The word 'or' in the mahr phrase 'a horse or a donkey' is here for diversification (تنويع), meaning the husband can choose either. It does not indicate doubt between two specific animals. If it did indicate doubt, the ruling changes.
If 'or' indicates doubt, Abu Hanifa applies tahkeem (mahr al-mithl); the Sahibayn require the lower value.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the doubt scenario
When the husband says 'I marry you on a horse or a donkey' with doubt, Abu Hanifa holds that the specification is invalid due to uncertainty, leading to mahr al-mithl (tahkeem). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the husband must give the lower of the two values. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate disagreement within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى فرس أو حمار أي لو تزوجها على فرس فقط أو تزوج على حمار فقط يعني تزوج على حيوان ذكر جنسه دون نوعه فإنه مخير بين أن يسلم فرساً وسطاً وبين أن يسلم إليها قيمة الفرس الوسط، وليس المعنى أنه تزوجها على هذا أو هذا على معنى الشك والترديد، بل كلمة "أو " ههنا للتنويع، ولو تزوجها على فرس أو حمار بمعنى الشك والتردد بينهما، فالجواب فيه كالجواب في المسألة الأولى من تحكيم مهر المثل عنده، ووجوب الأقل عندهما، ولو تزوجها على حيوان ولم يبين جنسه بأن تزوجها على دابة بطلت التسمية، ويجب مهر المثل؛ لتفاحش الجهالة، وقال الشافعي: يجب مهر المثل في الوجهين جميعاً. [ رمز الحقائق: ٢١٤/١] لأن عنده ما لا يصلح ثمنا في البيع لا يصلح مسمى في النكاح؛ إذ كل واحد منهما عقد معاوضة، ولنا أنه معاوضة مال بغير مال فجعلناه بمنزلة التزام المال - يجب الوسط أو قيمته، وعلى ثوب أو لحمر أو خنزير أو على هذا الخل، فإذا هو من الفرس والحمار وغيرهما
And on a horse or donkey: meaning if he marries her on a horse only or on a donkey only, i.e., he marries on an animal mentioning its genus without its type, then he has the choice between giving a medium horse or giving its value. It does not mean that he married her on this or that with doubt and hesitation, rather the word 'or' here is for diversification. If he marries her on a horse or donkey with the meaning of doubt and hesitation between them, the answer is like the answer in the first issue: arbitration by mahr al-mithl according to him (Abu Hanifa) and obligation of the lower according to them (the two). And if he marries her on an animal without specifying its genus, such as marrying her on an animal (dabbah), the specification becomes invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib due to extreme ignorance (jahl). Al-Shafi'i said: mahr al-mithl is wajib in both cases. Because according to him, what is not suitable as a price in sale is not suitable as a named mahr in marriage, since both are contracts of exchange. And for us, it is an exchange of property for non-property, so we treat it like an undertaking of property - the medium or its value becomes obligatory. And on a garment or on wine or pig or on this vinegar, then it is from the horse and donkey and others.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when the mahr is a horse or donkey specified by genus without type. The husband has the choice to give a medium specimen or its value. If the 'or' indicates doubt between two specific animals, it falls under the earlier ruling of tahkeem (arbitration) with mahr al-mithl. If the animal is completely unspecified (e.g., 'an animal'), the specification is batil due to excessive jahl, and mahr al-mithl is wajib. The Shafi'i position is mentioned: they hold mahr al-mithl in both cases because they analogize nikah to sale regarding suitable countervalue. The Hanafi response: nikah is exchange of property (mahr) for non-property (manfa'ah of the wife), not a pure exchange of property, so the rules differ — the husband's undertaking is akin to a commitment to pay, and the medium is acceptable. The passage then transitions to the next set of cases (garment, wine, etc.) which will be covered in the next lesson.

Key Terms
وسط (wasat): The medium or average quality of the specified genus; not the best nor the worst.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man marries a woman on the mahr of 'a horse' without specifying type. According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is invalid due to uncertainty.
B) The husband must give a thoroughbred racehorse.
C) The husband may give a medium horse or its value.
D) The husband must give mahr al-mithl.

Key Takeaway
When mahr is specified by genus only, the husband gives a medium specimen or its value, and the marriage is valid.

Mahr with Excessive Ignorance: The Unspecified Animal Case
Ruling on mahr with excessive ignorance and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between jahl mufahhish (excessive ignorance) and moderate ignorance in mahr specification, and state that complete lack of genus specification invalidates the mahr term and requires mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
Excessive ignorance in mahr (e.g., 'an animal' without genus) invalidates the specification and triggers mahr al-mithl.

This lesson examines the scenario where the mahr is completely unspecified by genus, such as 'an animal' (dabbah). Marghinani rules that such specification is batil due to jahl mufahhish (excessive ignorance), obligating mahr al-mithl. We also analyze the Shafi'i objection, which analogizes nikah to sale, and the Hanafi response that distinguishes the two contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and its degree of ignorance
The mahr is specified as 'an animal' (dabbah) without any genus. This is jahl mufahhish (excessive ignorance) because the genus is unknown, making the mahr totally uncertain.
Compare with the previous lesson where genus (horse/donkey) was specified – that was moderate ignorance.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The specification is batil (void). The marriage contract itself remains valid (sahih), but the mahr defaults to mahr al-mithl (the woman's fair mahr).
Mahr al-mithl is determined by the mahr of women of her father's family or similar status.
3
Present the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that in both cases (genus-only and unspecified), the mahr is unsuitable because it is not fit to be a price in a sale, analogizing nikah to sale as a contract of exchange.
Shafi'i requires mahr al-mithl in both cases.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: Nikah is an exchange of property (mahr) for non-property (manfa'ah, i.e., sexual enjoyment). It is not a pure exchange of property like sale. Therefore, the rules are more lenient. The husband's undertaking is analogous to a commitment to give property, and moderate uncertainty is tolerated.
This response is based on qiyas and the nature of the nikah contract.

Source Text

Four Cases of Faulty Mahr: Marriage Valid, Mahr al-Mithl Wajib
Analyzes four faulty mahr specifications with rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for each of the four faulty mahr cases and explain why the marriage remains valid and mahr al-mithl is wajib when the specification is invalid.

Core Idea
Faulty mahr does not invalidate marriage; the fasid condition is voided and the woman gets mahr al-mithl.

This lesson dissects four classical scenarios where the mahr (dower) specified in a marriage contract is defective. In each case, the marriage remains valid, but the mahr obligation changes. Understanding these cases will sharpen your ability to distinguish between valid and invalid conditions in a marriage contract and recognise the Hanafi principles that preserve the contract's validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four cases
Read the Arabic text and list the four distinct scenarios: (1) a garment without description, (2) wine or pig as mahr, (3) a jar thought to be vinegar but is wine, (4) a slave thought to be a slave but is free.
Each case raises a different issue of ignorance (jahl), prohibition (haram), or impossibility (ta'dhir al-taslim).
2
Determine the ruling for each case
For each case, decide: Is the marriage valid? What mahr is owed? The common thread is that marriage is sahih in all cases, and the mahr is either mahr al-mithl (average dower) or a specific alternative.
Case (2) involves a condition to give a prohibited substance; marriage is not invalidated by such conditions.
3
Understand the reasoning behind each ruling
Analyse the specific proof or principle used: (1) ignorance of genus triggers mahr al-mithl; (2) fasid conditions do not nullify nikah (unlike sale); (3) ishaarah (indication) overrides tasmiah (naming) per Abu Hanifa; (4) when the named is of the same genus as the indicated, the contract attaches to the indicated entity, but if he is free the specification fails.
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf in cases (3) and (4).
4
Note the intra-madhhab differences
In the vinegar case, Abu Hanifa says mahr al-mithl; the Sahibayn say she gets its weight in vinegar. In the slave case, all say mahr al-mithl except Abu Yusuf who says value of a slave. Understand each position's basis.
The mufta bihi in the vinegar case is Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Apply the general principle
Generalise: When a condition in a marriage contract is fasid but not against the essence of marriage, the condition is void and the contract stands. The mahr is then determined by default rules (mahr al-mithl or mithl of the named item if deliverable).
This principle distinguishes nikah from sale, where a fasid condition invalidates the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى ثوب هذه أربع مسائل: إحداها : رجل تزوج امرأة على ثوب غير موصوف بأن ذكر الثوب ولم يذكر جنسه ولا وصفه، فإنه يجب مهر المثل؛ لأن هذه جهالة الجنس، ولو سمى جنساً بأن قال: هروي أو مروي تصح التسمية، ويجب الوسط، ويخير الزوج بين دفع المسمى وبين دفع قيمته وأيهما أدى تجبر المرأة على القبول، والمسألة الثانية: أنه تزوجها على خمر أو خنزير فالنكاح جائز والواجب مهر المثل؛ لأن شرط قبول الخمر والخنزير شرط فاسد والنكاح لا يفسد بالشروط الفاسدة، وقال مالك: يفسد النكاح كالبيع، قلنا: البيع يفسد بالشرط الفاسد، والمسألة الثالثة: أنه تزوجها على هذا الدن من الخل فإذا هو خمر، فإنه يصح النكاح، ويجب مهر المثل عند أبي حنيفة وقالا لها مثل وزنها خلاً؛ لأنه سمى مالاً وعجز عن تسليمه الآن، فيجب قيمته أو مثله، والخل من المثليات فيجب مثلها. وله: أن الإشارة والتسمية متى اجتمعتا فالعبرة للإشارة؛ لأنها أبلغ في التعريف فصار كأنه تزوجها على عياناً فيلغو التسمية ويجب مهر المثل، والمسألة الرابعة: أنه لو تزوجها على هذا العبد فإذا هو حر، يصح النكاح ويجب مهر المثل عند الطرفين، وقال أبو يوسف: تحب قيمته لو كان عبداً، والدليل ما تقدم في المسألة الثالثة؛ إلا أن محمداً يقول: إن المسمى إذا كان من جنس المشار إليه يتعلق العقد بوجوده في المشار إليه ذاتاً، والوصف تابع له، وإن كان المسمى خلاف جنس المشار إليه يتعلق العقد بالمسمى؛ لأن المسمى مثل المشار إليه وليس بتابع له، ويجب مهر المثل في العبد والمثل في الخمر؛ لأن العبد والحر جنس واحد؛ لقلة التفاوت في المنافع، والخمر والخل جنسان؛ لفحش التفاوت في المقاصد. (عيني ومستخلص)
And on a garment: these are four issues. First: a man marries a woman on an undescribed garment, mentioning the garment but not its type nor quality, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory because this is ignorance of genus. If he names a type, saying 'Harawi' or 'Marawi', the specification is valid and the medium is wajib, and the husband has the choice between giving the named or its value; whichever he gives, the woman is compelled to accept. Second issue: he marries her on wine or pig; the marriage is permissible and the wajib is mahr al-mithl because the condition of accepting wine/pig is a fasid condition, and marriage is not invalidated by fasid conditions. Malik said: the marriage is invalidated like sale. We said: sale is invalidated by a fasid condition. Third issue: he marries her on this jar of vinegar, and it turns out to be wine; the marriage is valid, and mahr al-mithl is wajib according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: she gets its weight in vinegar because he named property and is unable to deliver it now, so its value or its like is wajib, and vinegar is among mithliyat, so its like is wajib. And for him (Abu Hanifa): when indication and naming come together, the indication takes precedence because it is stronger in identification; so it is as if he married her on an eye-witnessed thing, so the naming is void and mahr al-mithl is wajib. Fourth issue: he marries her on this slave and he turns out to be free; the marriage is valid and mahr al-mithl is wajib according to both parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad? Actually 'al-tarafayn' means both sides). Abu Yusuf said: its value had he been a slave is owed. The proof is what preceded in the third issue, except that Muhammad says: if the named is of the same genus as the indicated, the contract attaches to its existence in the indicated entity, and the description is subsidiary to it; if the named is of a different genus than the indicated, the contract attaches to the named because the named is like the indicated and is not subsidiary to it. And mahr al-mithl is wajib in the slave case, and the like (mithl) in the wine case, because a slave and a free person are of one genus due to little difference in benefits, while wine and vinegar are two genera due to great difference in purposes. (Ayni and Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage presents four distinct cases of faulty mahr specification. First, a garment without description: if only the word 'garment' is mentioned (no type, no quality), the specification is invalid due to jahl al-jins (ignorance of genus), and mahr al-mithl is wajib. If a specific type is named (like 'Harawi'), the specification is valid and the husband gives the medium or its value. Second, mahr of wine or pig: since these are not valuable property in Islam, the condition is fasid but the nikah remains sahih; only mahr al-mithl is wajib. Malik's view that it invalidates the marriage is rejected by analogy to sale: in sale, fasid conditions invalidate the contract due to its nature as pure exchange; in nikah, the primary purpose is not exchange, so fasid conditions are voided but do not nullify the contract. Third, a jar of vinegar that turns out to be wine: here, the indication (ishaarah) to the specific jar takes precedence over the verbal naming (tasmiah) according to Abu Hanifa. He argues that because the wife saw the jar and knew it had a liquid, her consent was based on that, not on the word 'vinegar'. Thus the naming is ignored and mahr al-mithl is wajib. The Sahibayn hold that since vinegar is a mithli (fungible), the husband must give its weight in vinegar because he named a specific item and is unable to deliver it. Abu Hanifa's evidence: when ishaarah and tasmiah conflict, ishaarah is stronger. Fourth, a slave who turns out to be free: here, all agree mahr al-mithl is wajib, but Abu Yusuf opinion is that the husband must pay the value of a slave (as if it were a slave). Muhammad distinguishes based on genus: slave and free are same genus (human), so the contract attaches to the slave's essence, and since he is free, the specification fails entirely, leading to mahr al-mithl. In the vinegar/wine case, the genera differ, so the naming dominates? Actually Muhammad's reasoning is that for same genus, the indication dominates; for different genera, the naming dominates. However, for the slave case, mahr al-mithl is still the result. For the wine case, Abu Hanifa's ishaarah leads to mahr al-mithl while Sahibayn give mithl (like) vinegar.

Key Terms
إشارة (ishaarah): Pointing to a specific physical object; in this context, the act of indicating the jar takes precedence over the verbal description of its contents.
تمليث (mithliyat): Fungible property that can be replaced by its like (mithl) in weight, measure, or count.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower similar to that given to women of the bride's status (family, age, beauty, etc.) when the specified mahr is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a man marries a woman with the mahr being a garment without any description, what is the ruling according to this passage?
A) The marriage is invalid because the mahr is unknown.
B) The marriage is valid, and the woman gets a garment of medium quality.
C) The marriage is valid, and mahr al-mithl is wajib.
D) The husband must specify the garment within 3 days.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, faulty mahr specification does not invalidate the marriage; the fasid condition is void and the woman receives mahr al-mithl unless a valid alternative is specified.

Mahr of Two Slaves When One Is Free
The author presents the Hanafi internal dispute on mahr when one of two specified slaves turns out free.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on mahr when one of two specified slaves is free, and explain Abu Hanifa's reasoning for not resorting to mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A valid named mahr prevents mahr al-mithl, even if only part is deliverable.

This passage from the Kanz al-Daqaiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: a man marries a woman with two specified slaves as mahr, but one turns out free. The key question: does the wife get only the slave that is actually his property, or does she also receive compensation for the free one? Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani each give different answers, rooted in their views on the role of the named mahr (musamma) versus mahr al-mithl.

Guided Path
1
State the core issue
Identify the scenario and the key question: when one of two mahr slaves is free, what is owed?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
The wife gets the actual slave, if at least ten dirhams; otherwise the husband completes ten.
3
State the Sahibayn's positions
Abu Yusuf: slave + value of free; Muhammad: slave + completion of mahr al-mithl.
4
Analyse the reasoning behind each
Abu Yusuf: the husband gave impression of delivering both; Muhammad: if both free, mahr al-mithl applies; Abu Hanifa: the named slave is valid property, so it suffices.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference in amounts: Abu Hanifa gives only the slave (min ten dirhams); Abu Yusuf gives slave + value of free; Muhammad gives slave + completion of mahr al-mithl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أمهر العبدين أي إن تزوجها على عبدين فإذا أحدهما حر فمهرها العبد إذا ساوى عشرة دراهم أو أكثر عند أبي حنيفة، وإن كان أقل يكمل لها العشرة، وقال أبو يوسف لها العبد وقيمة الحر المسمى على تقدير كونه عبداً؛ لأنه أطمع سلامة العبدين وعجز عن تسليم أحدهما فتجب قيمته، وقال محمد: لها العبد إلى تمام مهر مثلها وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأنهما لو كانا حرين لكان الواجب مهر المثل عنده، فكذا إذا كان أحدهما حراً يجب العبد وتمام مهر المثل، ولأبي حنيفة: أن العبد هو مسمى وصلح مهراً؛ لكونه مالاً ، فيجب العبد، ووجوب المسمى وإن قل يمنع وجوب مهر المثل [ رمز الحقائق: ٢١٤/١] (مستخلص)
And if he gives in mahr two slaves, i.e., he marries her on two slaves, and one of them turns out to be free, then her mahr is the slave if it equals ten dirhams or more according to Abu Hanifa; if it is less, he completes ten for her. Abu Yusuf said: she gets the slave and the value of the named free [slave] on the assumption he was a slave, because he gave impression of delivering both slaves and is unable to deliver one, so its value is wajib. Muhammad said: she gets the slave up to the completion of her mahr al-mithl, and this is a narration from Abu Hanifa, because if both were free, the wajib would be mahr al-mithl in his view; so likewise if one is free, the slave is wajib plus the remainder of mahr al-mithl. And for Abu Hanifa: the slave is named and is valid as mahr because it is property, so the slave is wajib, and the obligation of the named, even if little, prevents the obligation of mahr al-mithl. (Rumuz al-Haqaiq 1/214) (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage details the internal Hanafi dispute on a specific case: a man marries a woman with two specified slaves as mahr, but one is discovered to be free (hence not his property to give). Abu Hanifa's position: the wife takes the slave that is actually a slave, provided it is worth at least ten dirhams (which is the minimum amount for a valid mahr according to the Hanafi school). If the slave is worth less than ten dirhams, the husband must make it up to ten. Abu Yusuf: she takes the slave and also the value of the free one as if he were a slave (so she gets a total equivalent to two slaves). Muhammad: she takes the slave, and if the total value of the two (slave + hypothetically free's value) is less than her mahr al-mithl, the husband must complete her mahr al-mithl. Muhammad reports that this is also a narration from Abu Hanifa. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the existing slave is a valid mahr as property; mahr al-mithl only applies when no valid mahr is specified, but here a valid part exists. The minimum ten dirhams ensures the mahr is not trivial. The ikhtilaf shows different views on whether the failure to deliver a part triggers mahr al-mithl for the whole or just compensation for the missing part.

Key Terms
مسمى (musamma): The explicitly named mahr; in this case the slave that is actually a slave.
يكمل لها العشرة (yukammilu laha al-asharah): The husband must complete the mahr to ten dirhams if the slave's value is less, because ten is the minimum for a valid mahr.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr of a woman similar to the wife in status, used when no mahr is specified or the specified mahr is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man gives two slaves as mahr and one is free, what is the wife entitled to?
A) She gets the slave and the value of the free one.
B) She gets mahr al-mithl.
C) She gets the slave, and if it is worth less than ten dirhams, the husband completes ten.
D) She gets nothing and the marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
When part of a specified mahr is undeliverable, Abu Hanifa holds the deliverable part suffices as mahr, provided it meets the minimum value, barring mahr al-mithl.

Mahr al-Mithl in Fasid Nikah: Limited by Specified Amount
Ruling on mahr al-mithl in fasid nikah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on mahr al-mithl in a fasid nikah and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its limitation to the specified amount.

Core Idea
In a fasid nikah, mahr al-mithl is due only by intercourse and is capped at the specified amount.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a subtle point in the law of invalid marriages. While a valid marriage obligates mahr by contract, a fasid nikah does not, unless consummated. Even then, the amount due is limited by what was specified, contrary to a common analogy with invalid sales. We will unpack the ruling, the proof, and the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling as given in the matn: mahr al-mithl is wajib only upon actual intercourse (wat') and cannot exceed the specified amount.
This is the mufta bihi position of Imam Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
Note that Zafar, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagreed, holding that mahr al-mithl is due in full regardless of the specified amount.
Their reasoning is based on analogy with invalid sales.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Understand the qiyas: in a fasid sale, the buyer must pay the full market value; similarly, in a fasid nikah, the full mahr al-mithl should be due.
The opposing dalil is qiyas jali.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi refutation distinguishes: the benefit of the vulva (manafi' al-bud') is not property (mal), so it is not valued independently like goods in a sale. Its value is only by specification in the contract, and the contract's invalidity does not create an independent obligation beyond what was agreed.
The wife's consent to the lesser amount is also considered a waiver.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if specified mahr is 1,000 but mahr al-mithl is 2,000, the Hanafi ruling gives only 1,000; the opposing view gives 2,000.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي النكاح الفاسد إنما يجب مهر المثل بالوطء ولم يزد على المسمّى، ويثبت النسب والعدّة... (ط) بالوطء: [حقيقة في القبل لا بغيره كالخلوة. (ط)] أي إذا فرق القاضي بين الزوجين في النكاح الفاسد قبل الدخول فلا مهر لها؛ لأن المهر في هذا النكاح لا يجب بمجرد العقد؛ لأنه فاسد، وكذلك بعد الخلوة؛ لأن الخلوة مع فساد النكاح لا تكون صحيحة؛ لعدم ثبوت القدرة، أو لوجود المانع وهو الحرمة كخلوة الحائض، فلا تقوم مقام الوطء، وإنما يجب المهر باستيفاء منافع البضع، فإن دخل بها فلها مهر مثلها لا يزاد على المسمى؛ لأنها أسقطت حقها في الزيادة لرضاها بما دونها، فلا يجب، وقال زفر: يجب مهر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ كما في البيع الفاسد، فإنه مضمون بالقيمة بالغة ما بلغت، وكذا المستوفي بالنكاح، ولنا: أن المستوفي ليس بمال وإنما يتقوم بالتسمية بناء على العقد، وقد فسد العقد فيفسد ما بني عليه، وقالت الثلاثة مثل قول زفر، ولو لم يكن المهر مسمى، أو كان مجهولاً يجب مهر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ بالاتفاق.
And in the invalid marriage, mahr al-mithl is only obligatory by intercourse and is not increased above the specified (mahr). If the judge separates the spouses before consummation, there is no mahr for her; because mahr in this marriage is not obligatory by mere contract, as it is invalid. Likewise after khalwa (seclusion), because khalwa with an invalid marriage is not valid, due to lack of established ability or presence of prohibition, like the seclusion of a menstruating woman, so it does not stand in place of intercourse. Mahr is only obligatory by enjoyment of the vulva's benefits. If he had intercourse with her, she gets her mahr al-mithl, not exceeding the specified amount, because she waived her right to the excess by being satisfied with less. Zafar said: Mahr al-mithl is obligatory regardless of amount, as in an invalid sale, where it is guaranteed by the value regardless. The three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zafar?) agreed with Zafar. Our proof: The benefit enjoyed is not property; it is only valued by specification based on the contract, and the contract was invalid so what is built upon it is invalid. If no mahr was specified or it was unknown, mahr al-mithl is due by agreement.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq with commentary addresses the ruling of mahr al-mithl in a fasid (invalid) marriage. The ruling states that in a fasid nikah, the mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory only upon actual intercourse (wat') with the vulva, not by mere contract or khalwa (seclusion). If separation occurs before consummation, no mahr is due. The commentary explains that khalwa in a fasid marriage does not have the effect of intercourse because the necessary ability (qudra) is absent or a prohibition (like menstruation) exists. If intercourse does occur, the wife is entitled to her mahr al-mithl, but cannot receive more than the amount specified in the contract, even if the mahr al-mithl is higher. This is because by agreeing to the specified amount, she has waived any excess. Zafar ibn al-Hudhayl (a Hanafi scholar) disagreed, holding that mahr al-mithl is due irrespective of the specified amount, analogous to an invalid sale where the full value must be paid. The three (likely Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Zafar himself? Actually 'the three' here refers to Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zafar according to some commentaries; they agreed with Zafar's position. However, the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa's) is that the benefit of the vulva is not a property that is valued independently; its value is derived solely from the contract's specification. Since the contract was invalid, that specification is invalid, but the wife's consent to the lesser amount is binding. Therefore, she cannot claim more than the specified mahr. If no mahr was specified at all, or it was unknown, then everyone agrees that mahr al-mithl is due unconditionally.

Key Terms
النكاح الفاسد (al-nikah al-fasid): A marriage contract that is invalid due to a missing condition of validity (e.g., lack of witnesses), but not entirely void (batil).
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr equivalent to what women of her paternal family receive, considering various attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid nikah without specified mahr, after consummation, what is the wife entitled to?
A) No mahr
B) Mahr al-mithl regardless of amount
C) Mahr al-mithl but only up to the amount typical for her peers
D) The mahr she requested before marriage

Key Takeaway
In a fasid nikah, mahr al-mithl is due only by intercourse and is capped at the specified amount, but if unspecified, it is due in full.

Lineage and Waiting Period in Invalid Marriage
Ruling on nasab and 'idda in fasid nikah with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on nasab and 'idda in fasid nikah, identify the evidence for each, and explain the intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
In fasid nikah, lineage is established from intercourse, and 'idda begins at separation—both to protect the child and avoid confusion.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two critical consequences of a fasid (invalid) marriage: the lineage of any child born and the wife's waiting period. The Hanafi school treats the invalid marriage like a valid one in such precautionary matters. However, there are notable internal differences on the precise timing. This lesson will guide you through the rulings, proofs, and the relied-upon positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues and their rulings
The passage deals with nasab (lineage) and 'idda (waiting period). For nasab, it is established in a fasid marriage as a precaution. For 'idda, it becomes obligatory if intercourse occurred.
Note that the ruling on nasab is a declaratory ruling, while 'idda is a wajib act on the woman.
2
Locate the proofs for each ruling
For nasab, the proof is the principle of precaution (ihtiyat) to preserve the child's life. For 'idda, the proof is that the invalid marriage is analogized to a valid one in precautionary matters, and the evidence from hadd (fixed punishment) after separation supports it.
The proof for 'idda is based on the concept of shubha (semblance) and the need to avoid confusion of lineage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for each proof
For nasab: precaution requires establishing lineage whenever possible, even from a fasid contract, to prevent the child from being lost. For 'idda: the semblance of marriage (shubha) creates the need for 'idda, and that semblance ends at separation—thus 'idda begins then.
Zafar's objection that 'idda should start from the last intercourse is countered by the fact that the shubha continues until separation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi differences
For nasab, Imam Muhammad holds that lineage is established from the time of intercourse (al-dukhul); the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold from the time of the contract. For 'idda, the school holds from separation; Zafar holds from the last intercourse.
The text indicates that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view for nasab, and the majority view for 'idda.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position: nasab is established from the time of intercourse; 'idda begins at the time of separation (either by husband's declaration or judge's order).
This ensures consistency: the child's lineage is secured from the earliest possible moment, while the woman's 'idda starts when the marriage semblance ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويثبت النسب [ أي نسب الولد المولود في النكاح الفاسد للاحتياط وتعتبر مدة النسب من وقت الدخول عند محمد وعليه الفتوى] في النكاح الفاسد من وقت الدخول عند محمد وعليه الفتوى ومن وقت النكاح عند الشيخين، وجه الثبوت أن النسب مما يحتاط في إثباته إحياء للولد؛ لأنه لم يوجد من يربيه فيترتب على الثابت من وجه وهو النكاح الفاسد ولا توارث بين الزوجين في النكاح الفاسد والموقوف. (مستخلص) والعدة : [ أي وتجب العدة إذا دخل بها؛ لأن الفاسد ملحق بالصحيح في موضع الاحتياط ويعتبر ابتداؤها من وقت التفريق. (ع)] أي وتجب العدة إقامة للشبهة مقام الحقيقة في موضع الاحتياط تحرزاً عن اشتباه النسب، ثم اعتبار ابتداء العدة عندنا من وقت التفريق عند القاضي، وقال زفر عليه: من آخر الوطيات؛ لأن العدة بسبب الوطء فيعتبر وجوب آخر الوطيات حتى لو حاضت بعد الوطء قبل التفريق ثلاث حيض فقد انقضت عدتها، ولنا: أنها تحب باعتبار شبهة النكاح، ووقع هذه الشبهة بالتفريق، ألا ترى أنه لو وطيها قبل التفريق لا يجب الحد ويجب بعده، والطلاق لا يتحقق في النكاح الفاسد، بل التفريق فيه متاركة من الزوج أو تفريق من القاضي، ولا يتحقق المتاركة إلا بالقول بأن يقول: "تاركتك" أو "خليت سبيلك", وعلم غير المتارك ليس بشرط لصحة المتاركة على الأصح كما في النكاح الصحيح، وإنكار النكاح إن كان بحضرتها فهو متاركة وإلا فلا، روي ذلك عن أبي يوسف.
And lineage is established (i.e., the lineage of the child born in the fasid marriage, as a precaution, and the period of lineage is considered from the time of intercourse according to Muhammad, and the fatwa is upon that) in the fasid marriage from the time of intercourse according to Muhammad, and from the time of marriage according to the two Shaykhs. The reason for establishment is that lineage is a matter where precaution is taken to preserve the child's life, because there is no one to raise him, so it is based on what is established from one aspect, which is the fasid marriage. And there is no inheritance between spouses in the fasid and suspended marriage. And the 'idda (waiting period): it is obligatory if he had intercourse with her, because the invalid is attached to the valid in matters of precaution, and its beginning is considered from the time of separation. We (Hanafis) consider the beginning from the time of separation by the judge. Zafar said: from the last intercourse, because the 'idda is due to intercourse, so the last intercourse is considered. Even if she menstruated after intercourse before separation three times, her 'idda would be complete. Our proof: it is due based on the semblance of marriage, and this semblance occurs at separation. Do you not see that if he had intercourse with her before separation, no hadd is required, but after separation it is required. Divorce does not occur in fasid marriage; rather, separation is forsaking by the husband or separation by the judge. Forsaking is only realized by saying 'I forsake you' or 'I release you', and the knowledge of the other is not a condition for the validity of forsaking according to the most correct view, as in a valid marriage. Denial of marriage if in her presence is forsaking, otherwise not. That is narrated from Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage deals with two related issues in a fasid (invalid) marriage: lineage (nasab) and waiting period ('idda). For nasab, the child born from a fasid marriage has his lineage established as a precautionary measure to preserve his life. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars regarding from when this lineage is calculated: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani says from the time of intercourse (al-dukhul), and the fatwa is given on this view. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) said from the time of the marriage contract. The reasoning is that nasab is cautiously established. However, note that there is no inheritance between spouses in a fasid or suspended (mawquf) marriage. For 'idda, if intercourse occurred, the wife must observe an 'idda (waiting period) because the invalid marriage is treated like a valid one in matters requiring precaution to avoid confusion of lineage. The beginning of the 'idda, according to the Hanafi school, is from the time of judicial separation (tafriq) ordered by the judge. Zafar held that it begins from the last intercourse. The Hanafi proof is that the 'idda is due because of the semblance (shubha) of marriage, and that semblance is severed at separation. Evidence: before separation, if he had intercourse, there is no hadd (punishment for zina), but after separation, hadd becomes due. Since divorce does not exist in a fasid marriage, separation is either the husband's declaration (mutaraka) or the judge's order. The husband's declaration must be explicit ('I forsake you' or 'I release you'), and it is valid even if the wife does not hear it. If the husband denies the marriage in her presence, that counts as forsaking; otherwise not.

Key Terms
النسب (al-nasab): Lineage or parentage of a child; established in fasid nikah as a precaution.
العدة (al-'idda): The waiting period a woman must observe after separation or death of husband.
الشبهة (al-shubha): Semblance or resemblance; in fiqh, a situation that creates doubt about the legality of an act, often used to avoid hadd or establish 'idda.
التفريق (al-tafriq): Separation; in fasid marriage, it is the event that ends the shubha and triggers 'idda.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (al-fatwa), from when is the nasab of a child born in a fasid marriage established?
A) From the time of the marriage contract
B) From the time of intercourse
C) From the time of separation
D) Only if the child is acknowledged by both parents

Key Takeaway
In a fasid marriage, the child's lineage is established from the time of intercourse, and the wife's 'idda begins at separation, both based on precaution.

Calculating Mahr al-Mithl: Hanafi Order of Reference and Attributes
Definition and criteria for calculating mahr al-mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the primary basis for calculating mahr al-mithl, list the fifteen attributes used for equivalence, and apply the hierarchical fallback order (paternal relatives → maternal relatives → strangers).

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl is based on the mahr of the woman's paternal female relatives, matched across fifteen specific traits, with a clear fallback hierarchy.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a woman marries without a specified mahr or with an invalid mahr, she is entitled to mahr al-mithl – the proper mahr. This lesson unpacks the precise method for calculating that amount: it begins with the mahr of women from her father's family, requiring equivalence in fifteen detailed attributes. Understanding this hierarchy ensures the mahr is fair and avoids arbitrary decisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Primary Reference Group
The text states that mahr al-mithl is 'considered by her paternal relatives' (qawm abiha). This includes women from the father's side: paternal aunts, cousins, sisters. Note that the maternal side is not considered unless the mother herself is from the father's lineage (e.g., a paternal cousin).
The proof cited is Ibn Mas'ud's saying: 'Her mahr is like that of her women.'
2
List the Fifteen Attributes of Equivalence
The passage lists fifteen traits in which the woman must be equivalent to her paternal female relatives: age, beauty, wealth, country, time (era), intellect, religion, knowledge, manners, piety, jurisprudence, perfection of character, youth, virginity, and that she has no child. However, some jurists note that not all fifteen can always be found, so the existing ones are used.
These attributes vary by time and culture; the principle is that mahr depends on factors that influence desirability.
3
Understand the Fallback Hierarchy
If no suitable paternal relative exists, the text says 'then from strangers.' However, the commentary clarifies that before turning to strangers, the mother's side should be considered if there is a similar woman from the mother's family (provided the mother's side is not from the father's lineage). The order is: paternal relatives → maternal relatives → strangers from the same tribe and country.
This hierarchy is based on the idea that a person is of the kind of their father's people, and in absence, the mother's people are closer than strangers.
4
Recognize the Testimony Requirement
The mahr al-mithl must be established by the testimony of two men or one man and two women. If no such testimony exists, the husband's statement with his oath is accepted. This ensures the amount is not arbitrarily set.
This is a procedural rule to prevent disputes.
5
Note the Intra-Madhhab Difference
Ibn Abi Layla argued that the mother's mahr should take precedence over the father's relatives, drawing an analogy to custody (hadhanah). The Hanafi response relies on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the principle that a person is connected to their paternal lineage. The mufta bihi is the paternal side first.
This ikhtilaf shows the importance of proof in juristic reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعتبر بقوم أبيها : [ أي بالنساء اللاتي من أقارب الأب كالعمات وبنات الأعمام والأخوات، ولا يعتبر بأمها إلا إذا كانت من قوم أبيها بأن كانت ابنة عم لا الأب. (ط،ع)] لقول ابن مسعود له في المفوضة: "لها نساءها"، مهر والظاهر من إضافة النساء إليها أنها باعتبار قرابة الأب؛ لأن الإنسان من جنس قوم أبيه، ولهذا صحت خلافة ابن . من إذا استوتا سنّاً وجمالاً ومالاً وبلداً وعصراً وعقلاً وديناً وبكارة، فإن لم توجد فمن الأجانب، وصح ضمان الولي المهر، من قوم أبيها فلا يعتبر بالمجنونة فلا يعتبر فالفاسقة أي من حيث البكارة والشرف، الأمة إذا كان أبوه قرشياً، وتعتبر المماثلة في خمس عشر خصلة: الجمال والحسب والمال والعقل والدين والعلم والأدب والتقوى والفقه وكمال الخلق وحداثة السن والبكارة وحال الوقت وحال الزوج وأن لا يكون لها ولد، وتعتبر هذه الأوصاف وقت التزوج، ويشترط أن يكون المخبر بمهر المثل رجلين أو رجلاً وامرأتين فإن لم يوجد من يشهد بمهر المثل فالقول فيه للزوج مع يمينه، فالقضاء بمهر المثل لا يصح إلا بالشهادة أو الإقرار. (فتح) إذا استوتا: أي المرأة التي يحكم لها بمهر المثل، والمرأة التي هي من قوم أبيها. رمز الحقائق: ٢١٥/١] سناً: أي من حيث السن صغراً وكبراً. (ط، ع) وجمالاً : أي من حيث الحسن، وقيل: لا يعتبر الجمال في بيت بل في أوساط الناس. (ع) وعصرا: أي من حيث العصر وهو الزمان. (ع) وبكارة ولو تزوجها بأزيد من مهر مثلها على أنها بكر فإذا هي ثيب لا تجب الزيادة، وظاهر كلام المصنف أنه يشترط التساوي في جميع هذه الأشياء؛ لأن المهر يختلف باختلاف هذه الأوصاف؛ لاختلاف الرغبات فيها، وقال ابن أبي ليلة: إن مهر أمها أولى بالاعتبار من قوم أبيها؛ لأنها جزء أمها حقيقة، وكذا قوم أمها اعتبارا بالحضانة ولنا ما روينا عن ابن مسعود اهل الله لكن في "شرح المجمع أنه إن لم توجد كل الأوصاف في قوم أبيها يعتبر الموجود فيها؛ لأن اجتماع هذه الأوصاف كلها في امرأتين متعذر، ولهذا لم يذكر بعض الفقهاء كونهما من بلد واحد، وبعضهم العقل والعصر، وبعضهم المال والجمال. (فتح، مستخلص) لم توجد من قوم أبيها من كانت مثل حالها في الأشياء المذكورة. (ط) فمن الأجانب : [ أي فيعتبر منهم لكن من قبيلة هي مثل قبيلة أبيها من بلدها. (ط، ع)] محمول على ما إذا لم يوجد من يماثلها من قوم أمها أيضاً، ولهذا نقل السيد الحموي أنه لا يعتبر بالأم وقومها مع قوم الأب لا أنها لا تعتبر تكون أدنى حالاً من الأجانب، فالاعتبار من : يماثلها من قوم أمها أولى من أن يعتبر بالأجانب. (فتح)
It is considered by her paternal relatives: i.e., the women who are relatives of the father, like paternal aunts, paternal cousins, and sisters. It is not considered by her mother unless she is from her father's people, e.g., if she is a paternal cousin. Based on the saying of Ibn Mas'ud regarding a woman with unspecified mahr: 'Her mahr is like that of her women.' The apparent meaning of 'her women' is by paternal kinship, because a person is from the kind of his paternal people. Therefore, the caliphate of a son is valid... If they are equal in age, beauty, wealth, country, time, intellect, religion, and virginity, then if not found, then from strangers. The guarantee of mahr by a guardian is valid. From her paternal relatives, so a mad woman is not considered, nor a sinful woman from the perspective of virginity and honor, nor a slave woman if her father is a Qurashi. Equivalence is considered in fifteen traits: beauty, lineage, wealth, intellect, religion, knowledge, manners, piety, jurisprudence, perfection of character, youth, virginity, current situation, the husband's situation, and that she has no child. These traits are considered at the time of marriage. It is required that the informant about mahr al-mithl be two men or a man and two women. If there is no one to testify about mahr al-mithl, then the statement is that of the husband with his oath. The ruling on mahr al-mithl is only valid by testimony or confession. Commentary: If they are equal: i.e., the woman being judged for mahr al-mithl and the woman from her father's people. Age: from the perspective of age, small or big. Beauty: from the perspective of beauty, and it is said that beauty is not considered within the family but among middle-class people. Time: from the perspective of time. Virginity: even if he married her for more than her mahr al-mithl on the understanding that she was a virgin, and she turned out to be non-virgin, the excess is not required. The apparent meaning of the author is that equality in all these things is required because mahr varies with these traits due to varying desires. Ibn Abi Layla said: The mahr of her mother is more appropriate to consider than her father's people, because she is part of her mother in reality, similarly her mother's people analogy to custody. Our proof is what we narrated from Ibn Mas'ud... But in Sharh al-Majma': if not all traits are found in the father's people, then the existing ones are considered because it is impossible to have all these traits together in two women. Hence some jurists did not mention being from the same country, some intellect and time, some wealth and beauty. If not found from her father's people someone like her in the mentioned things, then from strangers: i.e., they are considered but from a tribe similar to her father's tribe from her country. This is applicable when there is no one similar from her mother's people either; therefore al-Sayyid al-Hamawi transmitted that it is not considered by the mother and her people in the presence of the father's people, not that it is not considered at all when they are in a lower state than strangers. So the consideration from those similar from her mother's people is more appropriate than from strangers.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of how mahr al-mithl (the proper mahr) is calculated in Hanafi fiqh. The primary basis is the mahr given to women of the paternal family (qawm abiha), such as paternal aunts, cousins, and sisters. The maternal side is not considered unless the mother herself is from the father's lineage (e.g., a paternal cousin). This is derived from a saying of Ibn Mas'ud. The commentator emphasizes that a person is considered part of their father's people. The passage then lists fifteen attributes in which the woman seeking mahr al-mithl must be equivalent to the women of her father's family: age, beauty, wealth, country, time (era), intellect, religion, virginity, and others. If no such woman exists in the paternal family, then one looks to strangers (ajanib), i.e., women from the same tribe and country. However, if women from the mother's family exist and are more similar, they take precedence over strangers. The passage also addresses specific cases: a mad woman or sinful woman is not considered a match; a slave woman is not considered if the father is a Qurashi (since a free woman is of higher status). The testimony of two men or one man and two women is required to establish the mahr al-mithl; otherwise, the husband's statement with an oath is accepted. The commentator notes that it is impractical to require all fifteen traits exactly, so the existing traits are considered as much as possible.

Key Terms
قوم الأب (qawm al-ab): The paternal relatives of the woman, including paternal aunts, cousins, etc.
الأجانب (al-ajanib): Strangers; women unrelated to the woman, from the same tribe and country.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper mahr estimated by considering the mahr of women similar to the bride in certain attributes, typically from her paternal family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is determined by the mahr of the woman's paternal female relatives, matched across fifteen attributes, with a fallback to maternal relatives then strangers.
