(ع ، ط] حق التركيب "فلو" بالفاء دون الواو؛ لأن الواو توهم أن الشرط واصل والواصل لا يذكر له جواب وههنا الجواب مذكور، ويجوز أن تكون "لو" للوصل؛ لأن ذكر الجواب لا يمنع كون الشرط واصلاً وإن كان الأكثر عدم الذكر لكن جعلها للوصل يقتضي أن - مستنكر، فالقول لورثته، ومن بعث إلى امرأته شيئاً فقالت: هو هدية، وقال: هو من المهر، المعقود عليها أي المرأة أي المبعوث اهديتهالي أي الزوج فالقول له في غير المهيأ للأكل، ولو نكح ذمي ذميّة بميتَةٍ أو دم - قول المصنف : القول" "لورثته يشعر أنه لا فرق فيه بين أن يكون الاختلاف في القدر أو الأصل وليس كذلك فتعين التعبير بالفاء بدل الواو أو حذف الواو أصلا. (مسكين، فتح) قدر المهر: بأن قالت ورثة الزوج: المهر ألف وقالت ورثة الزوجة بل ألفان (ع) فالقول لورثته [ أي لورثة الزوج ولا يحكم بمهر المثل. (ط ، ع)] هذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعند أبي يوسف القول قول ورثة الزوج فيما أقروا به، إلا أن يأتوا بشيء قليل، وعند محمد: القول قول ورثة المرأة إلى تمام مهر مثلها، ولورثة الزوج فيما ما زاد على مهر المثل كما في حال الحياة وإن اختلفوا في أصل التسمية بعد موتهما، فعند الإمام القول لمن ينكر التسمية، ولا يقضى بشيء، وعندهما يقضى بمهر المثل كما في حال الحياة وعليه ،الفتوى، وإذا مات الزوجان وقد سمي لها مهراً فلورثتها أن يأخذوا ذلك من تركة الزوج، وإن لم يكن سمي لها مهراً فلا شيء لورثتها عنده، وعندهما لورثتها المسمى في الوجه الأول، ومهر المثل في الثاني ثم اعلم أن المستحق بالنكاح ثلاثة أشياء: المهر المسمى: وهو أقواها والنفقة وهي أضعفها ومهر المثل وهو المتوسط، فالأقوى لا يسقط بالموت، والأضعف يسقط بموت أحدهما، والمتوسط يسقط بموتهما لا بموت أحدهما. (مسكين، فتح)
And if concerning the original specification [meaning they differed while alive, one denied the specification and the other claimed it (T)] i.e., if they differed on the original specification, whether the difference occurred during their lifetimes or after the death of one of them. And if the difference occurred after divorce before consummation, mut'ah is obligatory; because that is the original ruling according to both parties, and according to the second [i.e., the Sahibayn], judgment by the specified amount is impossible, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory by consensus. As for according to them (the Sahibayn), it is apparent; because one claims specification and the other denies, so the statement is of the denier. Similarly according to Abu Yusuf, due to the impossibility of judgment by the specified amount. And if the difference occurred after the death of one of them, such that the living person differs with the heirs of the deceased, then the answer is the same as during their lifetimes while the marriage was in effect, in both the original and amount by agreement; because the consideration of mahr al-mithl does not fall away with the death of one of them. Similarly, if he divorced her after consummation, then if the difference between the living and the heirs of the deceased is about the original, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, and if the difference is about the amount, mahr al-mithl is judged. (Fath) And if both die, meaning the two spouses, and their heirs differ. (T) And if concerning the amount of mahr, it is connected to what preceded, i.e., if their difference is about the amount of mahr. (A, T) The correct construction is 'falau' with fa not waw; because waw would suggest that the condition is connected and the connected does not have a response, but here the response is mentioned. It is permissible that 'lau' is for connection, because mentioning the response does not preclude the condition being connected, although the majority do not mention it. But making it for connection requires that it be repugnant. Then the statement is for his heirs. And if someone sends to his wife something, and she says: it is a gift, and he says: it is from the mahr, the contracted upon her (i.e., the woman, i.e., the sent item, he gave it to me, i.e., the husband), then the statement is his regarding items not prepared for eating. And if a dhimmi marries a dhimmiyyah with carrion or blood - the author's statement: 'the statement is for his heirs' suggests there is no difference between whether the dispute is about the amount or the original, and it is not so; therefore it is necessary to use the particle fa instead of waw or to delete the waw entirely. (Miskin, Fath) Amount of mahr: that is, if the heirs of the husband say: the mahr is one thousand, and the heirs of the wife say rather two thousand (A), then the statement is for his heirs [i.e., the heirs of the husband, and mahr al-mithl is not judged (T, A)]. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, the statement is the statement of the heirs of the husband regarding what they acknowledge, unless they bring something insignificant. According to Muhammad, the statement is the statement of the heirs of the wife up to the full amount of her mahr al-mithl, and the heirs of the husband have only what exceeds mahr al-mithl. And if they differ on the original specification after both have died, then according to the Imam, the statement is of the one who denies the specification, and nothing is judged; according to the Sahibayn, mahr al-mithl is judged as during life, and upon that is the fatwa. And if both spouses have died and a mahr was specified for her, then her heirs may take that from the husband's estate; if no mahr was specified for her, then nothing is due to her heirs according to him (Abu Hanifa). According to the Sahibayn, for her heirs the specified mahr in the first case, and mahr al-mithl in the second. Then know that the entitlements by marriage are three things: the specified mahr, which is the strongest; maintenance, which is the weakest; and mahr al-mithl, which is intermediate. The strongest does not fall away by death, the weakest falls away by the death of one of them, and the intermediate falls away by the death of both, not by the death of one of them. (Miskin, Fath)
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage addresses disputes over the original specification of mahr (asl al-musamma) during life and after death. The matn line 'ولو في أصل المسمّى' is explained: if the spouses differ on whether a mahr was specified, the one denying it (the husband) is believed, and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory by consensus. After the death of one spouse, the same rule applies between the survivor and the deceased's heirs. When both die and heirs differ on the amount, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the heirs of the husband are believed and no mahr al-mithl is given; Abu Yusuf also believes the husband's heirs, but with a caveat for an unusually low claim; Muhammad believes the wife's heirs up to mahr al-mithl. The relied-upon fatwa (upon which fatwa is given) is that of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), where mahr al-mithl is judged if the original specification is denied. The passage concludes with a hierarchy: specified mahr is strongest (survives death of either), maintenance is weakest (falls by death of either), and mahr al-mithl is intermediate (falls only when both die).

Key Terms
أصل المسمى (asl al-musamma): The original specification of the mahr at the time of marriage; whether a specific amount or item was named as dower.
المهر المسمى (al-mahr al-musamma): The specifically named dower agreed upon at the marriage contract.
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance provided by the husband to the wife during marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the text, if both spouses die and their heirs differ on the original specification of mahr, what is the ruling?
A) Nothing is due
B) Mahr al-mithl is judged
C) The heir of the husband is believed without mahr
D) The heir of the wife is believed without condition

Key Takeaway
When the specified mahr is denied, mahr al-mithl is wajib by consensus; after both die, the mufta bihi is that mahr al-mithl is still judged.

Husband's Gift vs Mahr: Determining Whose Statement is Accepted
Ruling on dispute when husband sends items to wife: gift vs mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for whose statement is accepted when a husband and wife dispute over items sent, and apply the distinction between perishable and non-perishable goods.

Core Idea
For perishable items, the wife's claim of gift is accepted; for durable goods, the husband's claim of mahr prevails.

A common marital dispute arises when a husband sends items to his wife and later claims they were part of the mahr, while the wife insists they were gifts. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on which party's statement is credited, based on the nature of the items and customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the parties
The husband sends items (e.g., money, cloth, food) to his wife. She claims they are gifts; he claims they are part of the mahr (dower). Each has an interest: if it's mahr, the husband reduces his debt; if it's a gift, the wife keeps the item without reducing mahr.
The dispute is about the intention behind the transfer.
2
Determine the type of item
Categorize the item as either 'prepared for eating' (perishable, e.g., meat, bread, fresh fruit) or 'not prepared for eating' (durable, e.g., honey, walnuts, cloth, a living sheep).
Customary practice is key: perishable items are typically given as gifts, so the wife is believed.
3
Apply the rule based on the item type
For non-perishable items, the husband's statement is accepted with his oath. For perishable items, the wife's statement is accepted with her oath, because custom indicates such items are gifts.
The rule derives from the principle that the giver knows his intention, but custom overrides for food.
4
Understand the consequences after the oath
If the husband swears (for non-perishable) and the item still exists, the wife must return it and can claim the remaining mahr. If destroyed, she returns its like if it's a fungible (mithli); otherwise no return is required. If the wife swears (for perishable), the item is hers and does not reduce the mahr.
Fungible goods have equivalents in the market.
5
Recognize the custom rule for worn items and household goods
Items the wife is wearing (khimar, dress) and household goods cannot be counted as mahr, because custom treats them as gifts or personal property. The husband's claim regarding these is not accepted.
Faqih Abu al-Layth considered this the chosen (mukhtar) view.

Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage covers the dispute when a husband sends items to his wife and she claims they are gifts while he claims they are part of the mahr. The ruling is that the husband's statement is accepted with his oath for items that are not perishable (like honey, walnuts, clothes, a living sheep) because he is the giver and knows best the intention. For perishable items (like meat, bread, fruits), the wife's statement is accepted because custom indicates such items are usually gifts. If the husband swears and the item still exists, the wife may return it and claim the remaining mahr; if it is destroyed and it is a fungible (mithli), she must return its like; otherwise she does not have to compensate. The passage also notes that items the wife is wearing (like a khimar or dress) cannot be counted as mahr due to custom. This ruling is based on apparent circumstances and customary practice ('urf).

Key Terms
المهيأ للأكل (al-muhayya' li al-akl): Items prepared for immediate consumption, such as meat, bread, fresh fruits, which spoil quickly.
المثلي (al-mithli): A fungible good that has equivalents in the market, so compensation is by returning the same type and quantity.
القول له (al-qawl lahu): His statement is accepted (with oath). A procedural principle meaning that the party's claim is credited as evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) She may keep the item and the mahr is reduced accordingly.
B) She must return the item and can claim the remaining mahr.
C) She can keep the item but must pay its value.
D) She must return the item and forfeit any further mahr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes marital gift disputes based on custom: the husband is believed for durable goods, the wife for perishable and habitually gifted items.

Rulings on Mahr: Disputes and Non-Muslim Cases
Multiple rulings on mahr: disputes, heirs, and non-Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on mahr disputes between spouses and heirs, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in dhimmi mahr cases.

Core Idea
In mahr disputes, the husband's word prevails for durable goods; for perishables the wife's word holds; for dhimmis, mahr al-mithl is the relied-upon view.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents key rulings on mahr (dower) in marriage, covering three main areas: disputes between spouses about gifts vs. mahr, disputes among heirs after death, and the special case of non-Muslims marrying with invalid mahr. The Hanafi school has notable internal differences, with the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad often being the relied-upon view in later fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers disputes over mahr: (1) husband sends something, wife claims gift, husband says it's mahr; (2) heirs differ after both spouses die; (3) dhimmis marry with carrion, blood, wine, pig, or no mahr. Recognize each as a distinct legal question.
2
Apply the principle of custom (urf) to gift vs. mahr
For non-perishable items (honey, cloth), the husband's statement is taken because he is the owner and custom supports him. For perishable items (meat, bread), the wife's statement is taken because custom suggests they are gifts. This is a rule of evidence based on common practice.
The Faqih Abu al-Layth adds that items the wife is wearing or household goods cannot be counted as mahr without strong evidence.
3
Analyze heirs' dispute after death
If husband's heirs say mahr is 1000 and wife's heirs say 2000, Abu Hanifa gives statement to husband's heirs. Abu Yusuf also gives to husband's heirs unless they claim a very small amount. Muhammad gives to wife's heirs up to mahr al-mithl. The fatwa is according to the two companions: mahr al-mithl is adjudged.
The strongest element (named mahr) does not fall by death, nafaqah falls, and mahr al-mithl falls only if both die.
4
Understand dhimmi mahr rulings
For dhimmis marrying with carrion, blood, or no mahr, Abu Hanifa says no mahr is due because they follow their own religion. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say mahr al-mithl is obligatory because dhimmis are subject to Islamic transactional laws. For harbis, all three agree no mahr.
If dhimmi marries with specified wine or pig, then converts, Abu Hanifa gives the items; Abu Yusuf gives mahr al-mithl; Muhammad gives their value.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text states 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' for the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the heirs' dispute and presumably for dhimmi cases as well. Thus, in practice, a Hanafi judge would rule mahr al-mithl where applicable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح
باب المهر
فالقول لورثته، ومن بعث إلى امرأته شيئاً فقالت: هو هدية، وقال: هو من المهر، المعقود عليها أي المرأة أي المبعوث اهديتهالي أي الزوج فالقول له في غير المهيأ للأكل، ولو نكح ذمي ذميّة بميتَةٍ أو دم - قول المصنف : القول" لورثته يشعر أنه لا فرق فيه بين أن يكون الاختلاف في القدر أو الأصل وليس كذلك فتعين التعبير بالفاء بدل الواو أو حذف الواو أصلا. (مسكين، فتح) قدر المهر: بأن قالت ورثة الزوج: المهر ألف وقالت ورثة الزوجة بل ألفان (ع) فالقول لورثته [ أي لورثة الزوج ولا يحكم بمهر المثل. (ط ، ع)] هذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعند أبي يوسف القول قول ورثة الزوج فيما أقروا به، إلا أن يأتوا بشيء قليل، وعند محمد: القول قول ورثة المرأة إلى تمام مهر مثلها، ولورثة الزوج فيما ما زاد على مهر المثل كما في حال الحياة وإن اختلفوا في أصل التسمية بعد موتهما، فعند الإمام القول لمن ينكر التسمية، ولا يقضى بشيء، وعندهما يقضى بمهر المثل كما في حال الحياة وعليه ،الفتوى، وإذا مات الزوجان وقد سمي لها مهراً فلورثتها أن يأخذوا ذلك من تركة الزوج، وإن لم يكن سمي لها مهراً فلا شيء لورثتها عنده، وعندهما لورثتها المسمى في الوجه الأول، ومهر المثل في الثاني ثم اعلم أن المستحق بالنكاح ثلاثة أشياء: المهر المسمى: وهو أقواها والنفقة وهي أضعفها ومهر المثل وهو المتوسط، فالأقوى لا يسقط بالموت، والأضعف يسقط بموت أحدهما، والمتوسط يسقط بموتهما لا بموت أحدهما. (مسكين، فتح) شيئا من الدراهم أو الدنانير أو القماش ونحوها قبل الزفاف أو بعد ما بني هو من المهر: أي من بعض مهرك أو كسوتك أو عارية. (ط،ع) بها ثم اختلفا. (ط،ع) فالقول له : [ أي للزوج بيمينه؛ لأنه المملك فكان أعرف لجهة التمليك. (ع)] مع يمينه، فإن حلف والمبعوث قائم فلها أن ترده وترجع بباقي المهر ، وإن كان هالكاً فإن كان مثلياً ردت مثله، وإلا لم ترجع، وقوله: "في غير المهيأ للأكل" أي ما لا يفسد بالبقاء كالعسل والجوز ونحوهما وما يفسد بالبقاء كاللحم والخبز، فإن القول فيه قول المرأة، ولا يكون مهراً بحال؛ لأن الظاهر شاهد لها للعرف؛ ومن هنا قال الفقيه أبو الليث: المختار أن ما عليه من الخمار والدرع ونحو ذلك لا يقبل قوله فيه؛ لأن الظاهر يكذبه، وليس له أن يحسبه من المهر، وكذا متاع البيت لا يحسب من المهر. (مسكين، فتح) للأكل وهو ما لا يفسد ببقائه كالعسل والسمن والشاة الحية والثياب بخلاف المهيأ للأكل كاللحم والخبز والفواكه التي لا تبقي؛ فإن القول فيه قول الزوجة مع اليمين؛ الجريان العادة بإهدائها فكان الظاهر شاهداً لها. (ط،ع) ولو نكح ذمي: شروع في بيان مهور الكفار بعد مهور المسلمين، ولو عبر بالكافر ليعم المستأمن لكان أولى؛ لأنه كالذمي أي لو نكح ذمي بميتة أي بما ليس بمال أو بنفي المهر أو السكوت عن ذكره فدخل بها الزوج أو طلقها قبل الدخول أو مات عنها أو ماتت عنه فلا مهر لها عند الإمام؛ لأنا أمرنا بتركهم وما يدينون، فعنده = يعني في دينهم الوطء س م لها، وكذا الحربيان قمه، ولو تزوج ذمي دمية بخمر أو خنزير عين فأسلما أو أسلم أحدُهُمَا أي في دار الحرب لها الخمر والخترير، عند الإمام عين - يعني مشار إليه قبل القبض لا يجب شيء بدون اعتقادهم؛ لأنها لما رضيت بما ليس بمال ولا قيمة فقد رضيت بغير بدل؛ ولأنه لو وجب لوجب حقاً لله والكافر غير مخاطب به، ولا يجب حقاً لها لرضاها بدونه، وعندهما: يجب مهر المثل؛ لأن أهل الذمة التزموا أحكامنا في المعاملات والنكاح منها، ولهذا جرت عليهم أحكامه من لزوم النفقة والعدة وثبوت النسب والتوارث ،وغيرها وله أنهم لم يلتزموها فيما يعتقدون خلافه إلا ما شرط عليهم كبيع متروك التسمية؛ ولأن المهر حق الله بخلاف الأحكام التي ذكرت، ويجب عندهما المتعة إن طلقها قبل الدخول، وبه قال الشافعي وزفر، وإنما وضع المسألة في الذميين؛ لأن في المسلمين يجب مهر المثل إجماعاً، وقيد بالجواز؛ لأنهم إن اعتقدوا وجوب المهر حال ترك التسمية أو النفي يجب المهر. (عيني وفتح) أو بغير مهر : أي نكحها بغير مهر إما نفياه أو سكتا عنه. (ع) وذا جائز: أي والحال أن ذا أي النكاح بالميتة أو بغير المهر. (ط) أو مات الذمي عنها قبل الوطء أو ماتت عنه. (ط) لا مهر لها في الصورتين عند أبي حنيفة، ولو أسلما وترافعا إلينا. (ط،ع) وكذا الحربيان ثمه [ أي تعاقدا على ميتة أو دم أو على أن لا مهر لها. (ع)] أي في دار الحرب إذا نكحا إلخ لا مهر لها عند الثلاثة. أصحابنا، من وعند زفر: لها مهر المثل إن مات عنها أو دخل بها؛ لأن الخطاب عام، والنكاح لم يشرع بغير المال، ولهما: أن أهل الحرب غير ملتزمين أحكام الإسلام وولاية الإلزام منقطعة لتباين الدارين، بخلاف أهل الذمة؛ فإن أحكام الإسلام جارية عليهم ولأبي حنيفة أن أهل الذمة لا يلتزمون أحكامنا في الديانات وفيما يعتقدون المعاملات، ولهذا لا نمنعهم عن شرب الخمر وأكل الخنزير وبيعهما، وولاية الإلزام بالسيف والمحاجة، وكل ذلك منقطع باعتبار عقد الذمة، فإنا أمرنا أن نتركهم وما يدينون فصاروا كأهل الحرب. (فتح) بخمر أو خنزير عين: أي مشار إليهما، والتقييد به للاحتراز عن غير المعين منهما بأن جعلهما ديناً في الذمة، وقوله: "فأسلما" أي قبل القبض؛ لأن التفرقة بين المعين وغير المعين إنما تتأتى في هذه الحالة، أما بعد القبض فليس لها إلا ما قبضته ولو كان غير معين وقت العقد. (فتح) خلافه من لها الخمر والخترير: عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنها ملكتهما بالعقد، فتخلل الخمر وتسبب الخنزير، وقال أبو يوسف: لها مهر المثل، وقال محمد: قيمتهما، وهو قول أبي يوسف أولاً؛ لأن التسمية قد صحت وقت العقد، وقد عجز الآن عن التسليم، فتلزم القيمة، ولأبي يوسف أن المسلم منهي عن التمليك والتملك والتسليم والتسلم في الخمر والخنزير فيجب مهر المثل [رمز الحقائق: ۲۱۹/۱]
Book of Nikah. Chapter of Mahr. So the statement is given to his heirs. And whoever sent something to his wife and she said it is a gift and he said it is from the mahr, the contracted one meaning the woman, i.e. the sent one, I gifted it to her meaning the husband, so the statement is for him regarding what is not prepared for eating. And if a dhimmi married a dhimmi woman with carrion or blood... (continued) The author's statement: 'the statement is given to his heirs' suggests that there is no difference between dispute in the amount or the origin, but that is not so, so it is necessary to express with 'fa' instead of 'waw' or to omit the 'waw' altogether. (Miskeen, Fath) The amount of mahr: that the heirs of the husband said the mahr is one thousand and the heirs of the wife said it is two thousand, so the statement is given to his heirs [meaning the heirs of the husband and no nahr al-mithl is adjudged. (T, A)] This is according to Abu Hanifah. According to Abu Yusuf, the statement is given to the heirs of the husband regarding what they acknowledged, unless they come with something small. According to Muhammad, the statement is given to the heirs of the wife up to the full mahr al-mithl, and to the heirs of the husband regarding what is over the mahr al-mithl, as in case of life. And if they differ about the origin of the naming after their death, then according to Imam the statement is given to the one who denies the naming, and nothing is adjudged. According to them both, the mahr al-mithl is adjudged as in case of life, and upon it is the fatwa. And if the two spouses died and he had named a mahr for her, then her heirs take that from the husband's estate. If he had not named a mahr for her, then nothing is for her heirs according to him. According to them both, for her heirs is the named mahr in the first case and mahr al-mithl in the second. Then know that what is entitled in marriage are three things: the named mahr, which is the strongest, and nafaqah which is the weakest, and mahr al-mithl which is intermediate. So the strongest is not nullified by death, the weakest is nullified by the death of either, and the intermediate is nullified by the death of both but not by the death of either. (Miskeen, Fath) Something from dirhams or dinars or cloth and the like before the wedding or after it, he built with her, then they differed. (T, A) So the statement is given to him [meaning the husband with his oath; because he is the owner, so he is more aware of the aspect of ownership. (A)] with his oath. If he swore and the sent item is still present, then she can return it and go for the rest of the mahr. If it is destroyed, then if it is fungible she returns its like, otherwise she does not return. And his statement: 'regarding what is not prepared for eating' meaning what does not spoil by staying like honey, walnuts and the like, and what spoils by staying like meat and bread, then the statement is given to the woman, and it is not mahr at all; because the apparent evidence is for her due to custom. And from here, Faqih Abu l-Layth said: the chosen view is that what she is wearing like the khimar and the dress and the like, his statement is not accepted regarding it, because the apparent evidence belies him, and he may not count it as part of the mahr. Similarly, household goods are not counted as mahr. (Miskeen, Fath) For eating, and that is what does not spoil by staying like honey, ghee, a live sheep, and clothes, as opposed to what is prepared for eating like meat, bread, and fruits that do not remain; then the statement is given to the wife with the oath, due to the custom of gifting, so the apparent evidence is for her. (T, A) And if a dhimmi married: commencement of explaining the mahr of disbelievers after the mahr of Muslims. If he had used 'kafir' to include musta'min it would be better, because he is like a dhimmi. That is, if a dhimmi married with carrion, i.e. with something that is not property, or denying the mahr or being silent about it, then he consummated or divorced before consummation or she died or he died, there is no mahr for her according to Imam; because we are commanded to leave them and what they believe, so according to him... (continued) Similarly the two harbis. (q m h) And if a dhimmi married a dhimmi woman with specific wine or pig, then they embraced Islam or one of them embraced Islam, i.e. in dar al-harb, then she has the wine and the pig according to Imam, specific meaning pointed to, before possession. Nothing is obligatory without their belief; because she agreed to something that is not property and no value, so she agreed to a badal without something; and because if it were obligatory it would be a right of Allah and the disbeliever is not addressed with it, and it is not obligatory as her right because she is satisfied without it. According to them both, the mahr al-mithl is obligatory; because the dhimmis have undertaken our rulings in transactions, and nikah is among them, and therefore they are subject to its rulings of the necessity of nafaqah, iddah, establishing lineage, inheritance, and others. And it is said that they did not undertake them regarding what they believe contrary except what is imposed on them, like selling without naming the amount; and because the mahr is a right of Allah unlike the rulings mentioned, and mut'ah is obligatory according to them both if he divorced before consummation. Al-Shafi'i and Zufar also said this. The case was presented concerning dhimmis because regarding Muslims, mahr al-mithl is obligatory by consensus. And it is restricted to permissibility; because if they believe the mahr is obligatory at the time of omitting the name or denial, the mahr is obligatory. (Ayni and Fath) Or without mahr: meaning he married her without mahr, either they denied it or were silent about it. (A) And this is permissible: meaning the condition that this, the marriage with carrion or without mahr, is permissible. (T) Or the dhimmi died before consummation or she died. (T) There is no mahr for her in both cases according to Abu Hanifah, even if they became Muslim and came to us. (T, A) Similarly the two harbis then [i.e. they contracted with carrion or blood or on condition of no mahr.] (A) i.e. in dar al-harb if they married etc., there is no mahr for her according to the three of our scholars. And according to Zufar: she has mahr al-mithl if he died or consummated; because the address is general, and nikah is not legislated without wealth. And to them: the people of war are not bound by the rulings of Islam and the authority of compulsion is severed due to the difference of the two realms, unlike dhimmis; for the rulings of Islam apply to them. And for Abu Hanifah: the dhimmis do not undertake our rulings in religions and in what they believe regarding transactions, and therefore we do not prevent them from drinking wine, eating pork, and selling them, and the authority of compulsion by sword and argument, and all that is severed due to the dhimma contract, for we are commanded to leave them and what they believe, so they become like the people of war. (Fath) With specific wine or pig: meaning pointing to them, and the restriction is to avoid what is unspecified, i.e. if they make them a debt in the dhimmah. And his statement: 'they embraced Islam' i.e. before possession; because the distinction between specific and unspecified only occurs in this case. As for after possession, she only gets what she has taken even if it was unspecified at the time of contract. (Fath) Contrary to that, from him: she has the wine and the pig according to Abu Hanifah; because she owned them by the contract, so the wine becomes vinegar and the pig becomes pregnant? (?) And Abu Yusuf said: she has mahr al-mithl. And Muhammad said: their value. And this was the first statement of Abu Yusuf; because the naming was valid at the time of contract, and now he is unable to deliver, so the value is obligatory. And for Abu Yusuf, the Muslim is forbidden from owning, transferring, delivering, and receiving wine and pig, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/219]
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with interlinear commentary, presents several rulings related to mahr (dower) in marriage. The text is a ruling statement with expansion from sharh sources. The first ruling concerns disputes between spouses or heirs about the mahr. If a husband sends something to his wife, and she claims it was a gift while he claims it was part of the mahr, the husband's statement (with oath) is given weight for items that are not perishable (like honey, cloth). For perishable items (like bread, meat), the wife's statement is taken, as custom suggests gifts. The second ruling deals with disputes after the death of both spouses. If the heirs differ over the mahr amount, the husband's heirs' statement is given credibility according to Abu Hanifa (Imam), with the condition that the wife's heirs cannot claim more than mahr al-mithl. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad have slightly different views. The relied-upon position (fatwa) is that decided by the court. The third part addresses mahr in cases involving non-Muslims. If a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject) marries with an invalid mahr (carrion, blood, or no mahr), Abu Hanifa rules no mahr is due because the couple's own religion permits it. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that mahr al-mithl is obligatory, as dhimmis are subject to Islamic transactional laws. For harbis (enemy combatants), all three agree no mahr is due. In the specific case of marriage with wine or pig as specified items, if the couple then embraces Islam before taking possession, she gets the wine and pig according to Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf says mahr al-mithl; Muhammad says their value. The text always follows Hanafi hierarchy: Imam first, then Sahibayn, then the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
المهر المسمى (al-mahr al-musamma): The dower specifically named in the marriage contract.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman similar to the wife in her social standing and attributes.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim rule with a pact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a dhimmi marries a dhimmi woman with carrion as mahr and they do not convert, what is the ruling on mahr?
A) She is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
B) She is entitled to the value of the carrion.
C) She is not entitled to any mahr.
D) She is entitled to the carrion itself.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, mahr disputes are resolved based on custom and perishability, and for dhimmis the relied-upon view is mahr al-mithl, not the absence of mahr.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Mahr for Dhimmi Couple Without Specified Mahr
Dispute on mahr obligation for dhimmi couples after conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding mahr for dhimmi couples after conversion and identify the core reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
If a dhimmi woman marries without mahr, Abu Hanifa rules no mahr; the Sahibayn rule mahr al-mithl.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about whether mahr is due when a dhimmi couple marries without a specified mahr (or with a prohibited item as mahr) and later converts to Islam. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hinges on the legal capacity of dhimmis and the nature of the marriage contract. By the end of this lesson, you will not only know the ruling but also understand the legal reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
1. Establish the scenario
A dhimmi man marries a dhimmi woman without specifying a mahr (or with a forbidden item like carrion), which is permissible in their religion. They later convert to Islam and bring the case to a Muslim judge. The question: is mahr due?
This scenario is the basis of the dispute.
2
2. State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that no mahr is due because the woman consented to non-wealth, waiving her right. Also, if mahr were a right of Allah, disbelievers are not addressed by such obligations. Finally, she has no right because she was satisfied without it.
Abu Hanifa's reasoning focuses on the woman's consent and the status of dhimmis.
3
3. State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that mahr al-mithl is wajib because dhimmis have undertaken Islamic laws in transactions, and marriage is a transaction. They point to other marital rulings that apply to dhimmis (maintenance, iddah, inheritance). They also require mut'ah if divorced before consummation.
The Sahibayn analogize dhimmi marriages to Muslim marriages for transactional purposes.
4
4. Identify the condition and thamarah
The ruling assumes the couple considered the marriage permissible. If they believed mahr was obligatory when unspecified, then even Abu Hanifa would require mahr. The practical difference (thamarah) is that if they convert and come to a Hanafi judge, Abu Hanifa gives no mahr, while the Sahibayn give mahr al-mithl.
The condition reflects that the ruling depends on the couple's belief about the validity of the marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو بغير مهر وذا جائز عندهم فوطيت أو طلقت قبله أو مات لا مهر لها. لا يجب شيء بدون اعتقادهم؛ لأنها لما رضيت بما ليس بمال ولا قيمة فقد رضيت بغير بدل؛ ولأنه لو وجب لوجب حقاً لله والكافر غير مخاطب به، ولا يجب حقاً لها لرضاها بدونه، وعندهما: يجب مهر المثل؛ لأن أهل الذمة التزموا أحكامنا في المعاملات والنكاح منها، ولهذا جرت عليهم أحكامه من لزوم النفقة والعدة وثبوت النسب والتوارث، وغيرها، ويجب عندهما المتعة إن طلقها قبل الدخول، وبه قال الشافعي وزفر، وإنما وضع المسألة في الذميين؛ لأن في المسلمين يجب مهر المثل إجماعاً، وقيد بالجواز؛ لأنهم إن اعتقدوا وجوب المهر حال ترك التسمية أو النفي يجب المهر. أو بغير مهر: أي نكحها بغير مهر إما نفياه أو سكتا عنه. وذا جائز: أي والحال أن ذا أي النكاح بالميتة أو بغير المهر. أو مات الذمي عنها قبل الوطء أو ماتت عنه. لا مهر لها في الصورتين عند أبي حنيفة، ولو أسلما وترافعا إلينا.
Or without mahr, and that is permissible according to them, so if she is cohabited or divorced before that or dies, no mahr is due for her. Nothing is obligatory without their belief; because when she consented to something that is not property and has no value, she has consented to no compensation; and because if it were obligatory, it would be a right of Allah, and the disbeliever is not addressed by it, nor is a right due to her due to her consent without it. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), mahr al-mithl is obligatory; because dhimmis have undertaken our laws in transactions, and marriage is among them, and thus its rulings apply to them, such as obligatory maintenance, waiting period, lineage, and inheritance, etc. And according to the two, mut'ah is obligatory if he divorces her before consummation, and al-Shafi'i and Zufar said the same. He (the author) only placed the issue concerning dhimmis because for Muslims mahr al-mithl is obligatory by consensus. He conditioned it upon (their belief of) permissibility; because if they believe mahr is obligatory when specification is omitted or denied, then mahr is obligatory. 'Or without mahr' means he married her without mahr, either by negating it or remaining silent about it. 'And that is permissible' means that this marriage is with carrion or without mahr. Or the dhimmi dies before cohabitation or she dies. No mahr is due for her in both cases according to Abu Hanifa, even if they both convert and come to us.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding mahr for a dhimmi couple who marry without specifying a mahr or with a prohibited item (like carrion) as mahr, and then convert to Islam. The matn states the general ruling: no mahr is due. The commentary explains that, according to Abu Hanifa, nothing is obligatory because the woman consented to non-wealth, so she waived her right. Additionally, if mahr were due, it would be a right of Allah, and the disbeliever is not addressed by Islamic obligations in their original state. The two (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that dhimmis have committed to Islamic rulings in transactions, including marriage, so mahr al-mithl is due. They support their view by noting that other marriage consequences like maintenance, waiting period, lineage, and inheritance apply to them. The passage also notes that if divorce occurs before consummation, the Sahibayn require mut'ah (a consolatory gift), while Abu Hanifa's position (by implication) is that no mut'ah is due. This ruling is specific to dhimmis because for Muslims, mahr al-mithl is agreed upon when mahr is unspecified. The commentary then clarifies that the ruling assumes the couple considered it permissible in their religion; if they believe mahr is obligatory, then mahr would be due even according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of the Islamic state with a covenant (dhimma).
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equivalent dowry determined by the woman's status, due when specified mahr is invalid or missing.
متعة (mut'ah): A gift given to a divorced woman before consummation as consolation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is no mahr due for a dhimmi woman who married without mahr and then converted?
A) Because the marriage is invalid
B) Because she consented to non-wealth, waiving her right
C) Because Islam does not recognize dhimmi marriages
D) Because mahr is only for Muslims

Key Takeaway
The obligation of mahr for dhimmis after conversion is disputed within the Hanafi school, hinging on whether the marriage is treated as a transaction (Sahibayn) or as a private matter of consent (Abu Hanifa).

Mahr for Harbi Couple in Dar al-Harb
Ruling on mahr for warring non-Muslims in enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on mahr for a harbi couple in dar al-harb and evaluate Zufar's counter-argument.

Core Idea
No mahr is due for a harbi couple in dar al-harb because Islamic authority does not extend there.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of mahr when warring non-Muslims (harbis) marry in enemy territory without a valid mahr. The three primary Hanafi authorities agree on one ruling, but Zufar raises a principled objection. Understanding this dispute requires grasping how the Hanafi school conditions the applicability of Islamic rulings on political authority and jurisdiction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) from the text.
The text says 'no mahr for her'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Zufar disagrees and rules that mahr al-mithl is due if the husband dies or consummates.
Zufar was a student of Abu Hanifa, yet his opinion diverged here.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar's argument: the address of Islamic law is general to all humans, and marriage inherently requires wealth.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The three imams respond that harbis are not bound by Islamic rulings because the authority of enforcement is cut off by the difference of abodes.
They analogize to dhimmis but with a nuance: dhimmis are left alone in religious matters.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the husband dies or consummates, Zufar requires mahr; the Hanafi majority does not.
This affects real cases of harbi couples entering Islam later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا الحربيان أي تعاقدا على ميتة أو دم أو على أن لا مهر لها، أي في دار الحرب إذا نكحا لا مهر لها عند الثلاثة أصحابنا، من وعند زفر: لها مهر المثل إن مات عنها أو دخل بها؛ لأن الخطاب عام، والنكاح لم يشرع بغير المال، ولهما: أن أهل الحرب غير ملتزمين أحكام الإسلام وولاية الإلزام منقطعة لتباين الدارين، بخلاف أهل الذمة؛ فإن أحكام الإسلام جارية عليهم ولأبي حنيفة أن أهل الذمة لا يلتزمون أحكامنا في الديانات وفيما يعتقدون المعاملات، ولهذا لا نمنعهم عن شرب الخمر وأكل الخنزير وبيعهما، وولاية الإلزام بالسيف والمحاجة، وكل ذلك منقطع باعتبار عقد الذمة، فإنا أمرنا أن نتركهم وما يدينون فصاروا كأهل الحرب.
And likewise the two warring non-Muslims—meaning they contracted upon carrion, blood, or that there is no mahr for her, i.e., in dar al-harb, if they marry, there is no mahr for her according to our three associates. And according to Zufar, she has mahr al-mithl if he dies before her or consummates with her; because the address is general, and marriage was not legislated without wealth. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the people of war are not bound by the rulings of Islam, and the authority of enforcement is cut off due to the difference of abodes, unlike dhimmis, because the rulings of Islam are applied to them. And according to Abu Hanifa, the dhimmis do not undertake our rulings in matters of religion and what they believe regarding transactions, and for this reason we do not prevent them from drinking wine, eating pork, or selling them. And the authority of enforcement by sword and argument is cut off by virtue of the dhimma covenant, for we are commanded to leave them and what they believe, so they become like the people of war.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of two warring non-Muslims (harbis) in dar al-harb who marry with a prohibited mahr (like carrion or blood) or without specifying a mahr. The text states that all three Hanafi primary authorities—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad—agree that no mahr is due for her. Zufar, a Hanafi scholar from the earlier generation, disagrees and rules that mahr al-mithl is due if the husband dies or consummates. The reasoning for the Hanafi consensus is that harbis are not subject to Islamic rulings, and the authority to impose those rulings is absent due to the political boundary (difference of dar). The commentary then contrasts this with dhimmis, explaining that even though Islamic rulings apply to dhimmis in some matters, Abu Hanifa maintains that in religious beliefs and what they consider lawful transactions, they are left alone, much like harbis. Thus, for harbis, the Hanafi position is unanimous: no mahr is due.

Key Terms
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim not under Islamic protection, from a hostile territory (dar al-harb).
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory not under Islamic jurisdiction and with a state of hostility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Mahr al-mithl is due if consummated.
B) No mahr is due.
C) Mahr is due only if specified.
D) Mut'ah is required.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the obligation of mahr is contingent on Islamic legal authority; thus, no mahr is due from a harbi couple in dar al-harb.

Mahr for Dhimmi with Wine or Pork – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr when dhimmi converts before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on mahr when a dhimmi couple specifies wine or pork and converts before possession.

Core Idea
For a dhimmi marriage with wine/pork as mahr and later conversion, three Hanafi views diverge: Abu Hanifa gives the item (transformed), Muhammad gives qeemah, Abu Yusuf gives mahr al-mithl.

This lesson unpacks an intricate intra-Hanafi dispute that arises when a dhimmi couple specifies wine or pork as the mahr and then converts to Islam before taking possession. The ruling depends on whether the items are specific ('ayn) or non-specific (debt), and on which imam's view is followed. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how changes in legal capacity (from dhimmi to Muslim) affect existing contractual rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the contract
The case involves a dhimmi man marrying a dhimmi woman with wine or pork as the specified mahr (either specific items or as a debt). Both or one convert to Islam before possession.
The mahr is not inherently valid in Islamic law, but the marriage itself is valid because dhimmis are governed by their own laws initially.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa rules that for specific items, the wife gets the wine (which becomes vinegar) and the pork (which becomes tabooed, i.e., she cannot use it but it is her property). For non-specific, she gets qeemah (value) for wine and mahr al-mithl for pork.
He reasons that ownership was established at contract; conversion does not void ownership but transforms or prohibits the items.
3
State the Sahibayn positions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
Abu Yusuf ultimately holds mahr al-mithl for both specific and non-specific. Muhammad holds qeemah for both. These differ from Abu Hanifa and from each other.
Abu Yusuf's early view agreed with Muhammad, but he later retracted. Muhammad's view is consistent: since specification was valid at contract time, now delivery is impossible, so qeemah is due.
4
Analyze the proofs (dalil)
Abu Hanifa's proof: ownership via contract is not voided by conversion; items are delivered in transformed state. Abu Yusuf: Muslims are prohibited from dealing in wine/pork, so the specification is invalid; mahr al-mithl restores justice. Muhammad: specification was valid initially; now impossibility triggers qeemah.
These proofs reflect different views on whether the contract's validity is assessed at inception or at time of performance.
5
Apply to divorce before consummation
For divorce before consummation, Abu Hanifa gives half the specific item, half qeemah for non-specific wine, and mut'ah for pork. Muhammad gives half qeemah in all cases. Abu Yusuf gives mut'ah in all cases.
This shows how the same principles extend to partial mahr scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تزوج ذمي دمية بخمر أو خنزير عين فأسلما أو أسلم أحدُهُمَا أي في دار الحرب لها الخمر والخترير، عند الإمام أي للزوجة عين يعني مشار إليه قبل القبض لا يجب شيء بدون اعتقادهم؛ لأنها لما رضيت بما ليس بمال ولا قيمة فقد رضيت بغير بدل؛ ولأنه لو وجب لوجب حقاً لله والكافر غير مخاطب به، ولا يجب حقاً لها لرضاها بدونه، وعندهما: يجب مهر المثل؛ لأن أهل الذمة التزموا أحكامنا في المعاملات والنكاح منها، ولهذا جرت عليهم أحكامه من لزوم النفقة والعدة وثبوت النسب والتوارث، وغيرها ويجب عندهما المتعة إن طلقها قبل الدخول، وبه قال الشافعي وزفر، وإنما وضع المسألة في الذميين؛ لأن في المسلمين يجب مهر المثل إجماعاً، وقيد بالجواز؛ لأنهم إن اعتقدوا وجوب المهر حال ترك التسمية أو النفي يجب المهر. لها الخمر والخترير: عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنها ملكتهما بالعقد، فتخلل الخمر وتسبب الخنزير، وقال أبو يوسف: لها مهر المثل، وقال محمد: قيمتهما، وهو قول أبي يوسف أولاً؛ لأن التسمية قد صحت وقت العقد، وقد عجز الآن عن التسليم، فتلزم القيمة، ولأبي يوسف أن المسلم منهي عن التمليك والتملك والتسليم والتسلم في الخمر والخنزير فيجب مهر المثل. وفي غير العين لها قيمة الخمر ومهر المثل في الخنزير. أي ولها عند أبي حنيفة لها قيمة الخمر إلخ عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن ملكهما بطل، فيجب القيمة في الخمر، ومهر المثل في الخنزير؛ لأنه لا يمكن تسليم قيمته؛ لأنها مثله في ضمان العدوان وعند أبي يوسف: يجب مهر المثل كما في المعين، وعند محمد: تجب القيمة أيضاً، وإنما وجب لها قيمة الخمر عند الإمام؛ لأنه من ذوات الأمثال وليس أخذ قيمته كأخذ عينه بخلاف الخنزير؛ لأنه من ذوات القيم فأخذ قيمته كأخذ عينه، ولو طلقها قبل الدخول ففي المعين لها نصف العين عند أبي حنيفة، وفي غير المعين من الخمر لها نصف القيمة، وفي الخنزير لها متعة المثل، وعند محمد: لها بعد الطلاق نصف القيمة بكل حال، وعند أبي يوسف لها المتعة بكل حال. غير العين من الخمر والخنزير يعني إذا تزوجها على خمر غير معينة أو خنزير غير معين بأن جعلهما دينا في الذمة فأسلما قبل القبض أو أحدهما قبله.
And if a dhimmi marries a dhimmi woman specifying wine or specific pork, and they both convert or one of them converts, i.e., in dar al-harb, she has the wine and the pork according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), meaning for the wife as specific items before possession. Nothing is obligatory without their belief; because when she consented to something not property and without value, she consented without compensation; and if it were obligatory, it would be a right of Allah, and the disbeliever is not addressed by it, nor is a right due to her due to her consent without it. According to the two (Sahibayn), mahr al-mithl is obligatory; because dhimmis undertook our laws in transactions, and marriage is among them. They have the wine and pork: according to Abu Hanifa, because she owns them by the contract, so wine becomes vinegar and pork is tabooed. Abu Yusuf said: she has mahr al-mithl. Muhammad said: their value (qeemah), and that was Abu Yusuf's first position; because the specification was valid at the time of the contract, but now he is unable to deliver, so value is due. Abu Yusuf's later view: the Muslim is prohibited from ownership, giving and receiving of wine and pork, so mahr al-mithl is due. In the case of non-specific (wine/pork as a debt), she has the value of wine and mahr al-mithl for pork, according to Abu Hanifa; because ownership of both is void, so value is due for wine and mahr al-mithl for pork, because its value cannot be delivered as it is like it in tort liability. According to Abu Yusuf, mahr al-mithl is due as in the specific case; according to Muhammad, value is also due. If he divorces her before consummation, then for the specific item, she gets half the item according to Abu Hanifa; for non-specific wine, half the value; for pork, mut'ah al-mithl. According to Muhammad, she has half the value in all cases after divorce. According to Abu Yusuf, she has mut'ah al-mithl in all cases. Non-specific wine and pork means if he marries her on non-specific wine or pork, making them a debt in the dhimmah, then they convert before possession or one of them does.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage covers a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute when a dhimmi marries a dhimmi woman with wine or pork as the specified mahr (either specific items or as a debt), and then both or one converts to Islam before taking possession of the mahr. The matn states that Abu Hanifa rules she gets the wine and pork (if specific) because she owns them by the contract; after Islam, wine becomes vinegar (takhallul) and pork becomes prohibited (tasabbub). Abu Yusuf initially agreed with Muhammad that qeemah (value) is due, but later retracted to mahr al-mithl because a Muslim is prohibited from dealing in wine and pork. Muhammad consistently holds that qeemah is due because the specification was valid at contract time. For non-specific (in dhimmah) wine/pork, Abu Hanifa distinguishes: wine has a qeemah because it is from items of value, but pork's value cannot be given because it is like its substance in tort law; thus mahr al-mithl for pork. Abu Yusuf gives mahr al-mithl in both non-specific cases; Muhammad gives qeemah in both. For divorce before consummation, the rulings depend: Abu Hanifa gives half the specific item for mu'ayyan, half qeemah for non-specific wine, and mut'ah for pork. Muhammad gives half qeemah always. Abu Yusuf gives mut'ah always. The passage emphasizes that these rulings are specific to dhimmis because for Muslims, mahr al-mithl is given by consensus when mahr is invalid.

Key Terms
عين ('ayn): A specific, tangible item; here, wine or pork that is physically identified.
قيمة (qeemah): Monetary value or compensation due when specific item cannot be delivered.
متعة المثل (mut'ah al-mithl): A consolatory gift appropriate to the woman's status, given upon divorce before consummation when no fixed mahr applies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Abu Hanifa on non-specific wine as mahr when the couple converts before possession?
A) She gets mahr al-mithl
B) She gets the value (qeemah) of the wine
C) She gets the wine itself
D) She gets nothing

Key Takeaway
In a dhimmi marriage with wine/pork as mahr and subsequent conversion, the Hanafi school offers three valid views: item (transformed), qeemah, or mahr al-mithl, with Abu Hanifa's view being the primary one in the matn.

Mahr for Non-Specific Prohibited Items: The Three Hanafi Positions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr for non-specific wine and pig

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on mahr for non-specific wine and pig, and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind each position.

Core Idea
When dower is a non-specific prohibited item, Hanafi imams split between value and mahr al-mithl based on item type.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning marriage dower (mahr) when the specified item is non-specific (ghayr al-'ayn) and consists of wine or pig — both impermissible in Islamic law. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the views of the three leading Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Their disagreement stems from how they categorize these items — whether they belong to 'items of the same kind' (dhawi al-amthal) or 'items of value' (dhawi al-qiyam) — and the legal consequences of that categorization. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to follow Hanafi legal reasoning and to appreciate the nuanced application of qiyas within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The dower is specified as wine or pig, but not as a specific physical item; rather, it is a debt (dayn) in the dhimmah. The parties embrace Islam before delivery. The question: what does the wife receive as mahr?
This scenario arises because non-Muslims may marry with such dowers and later convert.
2
State the three positions
List each imam's ruling: Abu Hanifa: value for wine, mahr al-mithl for pig; Abu Yusuf: mahr al-mithl for both; Muhammad: value for both.
The matn (original text) gives Abu Hanifa's view; the commentary adds the Sahibayn.
3
Analyse the reasoning (ta'lil)
Identify the underlying principle: wine is from dhawi al-amthal (items of kind) — taking its value is not like taking the actual item; pig is from dhawi al-qiyam (items of value) — taking its value is equivalent to taking the item. This explains Abu Hanifa's distinction.
This is an example of qiyas with a nuanced distinction based on the nature of the item.
4
Apply to the divorce scenario
If divorce occurs before consummation, the rulings differ: for specific dower, half the item per Abu Hanifa; for non-specific wine, half the value; for pig, mut'at al-mithl. Abu Yusuf gives mut'ah in all, Muhammad gives half value in all.
Note how the pre-divorce rulings inform the post-divorce adjustments.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The differences affect what the wife actually receives. For example, in a case of non-specific pig mahr, she gets mahr al-mithl per Abu Hanifa, but value per Muhammad — potentially significant difference.
This shows how ikhtilaf within the school translates into different financial outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المهر
وفي غير العين لها قيمة الخمر ومهر المثل في الخنزير.
أي ولها عند أبي حنيفة
لها قيمة الخمر إلخ عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن ملكهما بطل، فيجب القيمة في الخمر، ومهر المثل في الخنزير؛ لأنه لا يمكن تسليم قيمته؛ لأنها مثله في ضمان العدوان وعند أبي يوسف: يجب مهر المثل كما في المعين، وعند محمد: تجب القيمة أيضاً، وإنما وجب لها قيمة الخمر عند الإمام؛ لأنه من ذوات الأمثال وليس أخذ قيمته كأخذ عينه بخلاف الخنزير؛ لأنه من ذوات القيم فأخذ قيمته كأخذ عينه، ولو طلقها قبل الدخول ففي المعين لها نصف العين عند أبي حنيفة، وفي غير المعين من الخمر لها نصف القيمة، وفي الخنزير لها متعة المثل، وعند محمد: لها بعد الطلاق نصف القيمة بكل حال، وعند أبي يوسف لها المتعة بكل حال. (عيني، فتح) غير العين من الخمر والخنزير يعني إذا تزوجها على خمر غير معينة أو خنزير غير معين بأن جعلهما دينا في الذمة فأسلما قبل القبض أو أحدهما قبله. (ع)
Chapter of Mahr. And for non-specific [dower], she has the value of wine and the mahr of the like for pig. That is, according to Abu Hanifa, she has the value of wine etc. according to Abu Hanifa because ownership of both was voided, so the value is obligatory for wine, and mahr al-mithl for pig because its value cannot be delivered because it is like it in the guarantee of transgression. And according to Abu Yusuf: mahr al-mithl is obligatory as in the specific [dower]. And according to Muhammad: the value is also obligatory. And it is obligatory for her the value of wine according to Imam because it is from items of the same kind and taking its value is not like taking its actual item, unlike the pig because it is from items of value, so taking its value is like taking its actual item. And if he divorced her before consummation, for the specific [dower] she has half of the specific item according to Abu Hanifa, and for non-specific of wine she has half of the value, and for pig she has mut'at al-mithl. And according to Muhammad: after divorce she has half the value in any case. And according to Abu Yusuf: she has the mut'ah in any case. (Ayni, Fath) Non-specific of wine and pig means if he married her on non-specific wine or non-specific pig by making them a debt in the dhimmah, and they embrace Islam before receipt or one of them before it. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of Mahr in Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the ruling when a marriage contract specifies a non-specific dower (i.e., not a particular item but a debt in the dhimmah) consisting of wine (khamr) or pig (khinzir). The matn states that for non-specific wine, the wife receives its market value, and for a non-specific pig, she receives mahr al-mithl (the dower of a woman of her status). The commentary expands on the positions of the three Hanafi imams. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that ownership of wine, being impure and valueless in Islamic law, is void, so the wife takes its value instead. For pig, since its value cannot be delivered (as it is also impure and not a permissible commodity), she takes mahr al-mithl. Abu Yusuf analogizes to specific dower and requires mahr al-mithl in both cases. Muhammad requires value in both. The difference stems from categorizing wine as 'items of kind' (dhawi al-amthal) where taking value differs from taking the item, while pig is 'items of value' (dhawi al-qiyam) where taking value is equivalent. The passage then covers the case of divorce before consummation: for a specific dower, she gets half of that specific item per Abu Hanifa; for non-specific wine, half its value; for pig, mut'at al-mithl (consolatory gift). Muhammad gives half value in all cases; Abu Yusuf gives mut'ah in all. The final clarification defines 'non-specific' as making the wine or pig a debt in the dhimmah, with both parties embracing Islam before payment.

Key Terms
غير العين (ghayr al-'ayn): Something unspecified and not a specific physical item; a debt in the dhimmah.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman of similar status to the wife, used when the specified dower is invalid.
القيمة (al-qimah): Market value of the item.
ذوات الأمثال (dhawi al-amthal): Items of the same kind; fungibles where the exact same type exists.
ذوات القيم (dhawi al-qiyam): Items of value; non-fungibles where value represents the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does Abu Hanifa rule for a non-specific dower of pig (khinzir)?
A) The wife gets the value of the pig
B) The wife gets mahr al-mithl
C) The wife gets half the value after divorce
D) The marriage is invalid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's ruling on non-specific wine and pig dower illustrates how differing categorizations of items (dhawi al-amthal vs. dhawi al-qiyam) lead to different outcomes within the school.

The Invalidity of Slave Marriage Without Master's Permission
States the general ruling and proof for slave marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's marriage without master's permission and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
A slave's marriage without permission is invalid and akin to fornication; permission is a condition for validity.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on slave marriage, clarifying that permission from the master is a necessary condition. The author addresses a seeming repetition from earlier and resolves it by explaining that 'not valid' means 'not executed'—the contract is suspended (mawquf). The proof is a clear hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him). A dispute with Imam Malik is also presented and rebutted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a slave (male or female) marrying without the master's permission. The Hanafi ruling is that the marriage is not valid (fasid) and specifically suspended (mawquf).
The author clarifies that 'not valid' means 'not executed', like the contract of a mediator.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith: 'Any male slave who marries without his master's permission is a fornicator.'
This is a Sunnah_ahad hadith with zanni thubut but qati dalalah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The term 'cahir' (fornicator) explicitly indicates that the marriage is invalid and tantamount to zina, implying that permission is required for validity.
The imperative for permission is deduced from the prohibition of zina.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik holds that a male slave can marry without permission because he owns divorce, so he owns marriage by analogy.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on qiyas.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The hadith is specific and overrides the analogy. The Hanafi position is relied upon due to the clear text.
The mufta bihi is that the marriage is suspended until permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب نكاح الرقيق الرقيق العبد والمملوك يطلق على الواحد والجمع فعيل بمعنى مفعول من الرق بمعنى الضعف سمي به المملوك لضعفه وكونه ممنوعا عن التصرفات لما فرغ من بيان نكاح الأحرار شرع في بيان نكاح الأرقاء وقدمه على الكافر لأن الإسلام فيهم غالب ومناسبة هذا الباب بباب المهر هي أن الرقيق يصلح أن يكون مهرا كما إذا تزوج رجل امرأة على رقيق وإذا كان الرقيق غير مشار إليه يجب لها الوسط أو قيمته ووسط الرقيق هو الحبشي والأدنى الأسود والأعلى الأبيض من هذا يتزوج بغير لم يجز إلى قوله إلا بإذن السيد هذه المسألة مكررة قد ذكرها المصنف فيما مضى بعبارة أحسن حيث قال ونكاح العبد والأمة بلا إذن السيد موقوف وههنا قال لم يجز فالأولى أن يقال لم ينفذ أو يقال إن عدم الجواز في المعاملات التي منها النكاح يكون بمعنى عدم النفاذ على أن ما ذكر في بابه استطرادا لا يعد مما ذكر قبله تكرار أو المعنى أنه يجوز لكنه لا ينفذ كعقد الفضولي وقال مالك يجوز للعبد أن يتزوج بغير إذن مولاه لأنه يملك الطلاق فيملك النكاح ولنا قوله عليه السلام أيما عبد تزوج بغير إذن مولاه فهو عاهر أي زان
Chapter on the marriage of slaves. The ‘slave’ is the male slave and the owned one, used for singular and plural, it is an intensive form meaning ‘acted upon’ from ‘al-riqq’ meaning weakness, so called because of his weakness and being prevented from dispositions. Having finished explaining the marriage of free persons, he began explaining the marriage of slaves, and gave it precedence over the disbeliever because Islam predominates among them. The connection of this chapter to the chapter on dower is that a slave can be given as dower, just as if a man marries a woman for a slave. And if the slave is not specifically identified, the medium slave or its value must be given; the medium slave is the Habashi, the lowest is the black, and the highest is the white. From this, [the ruling] that a slave marrying without permission is not valid up to his saying ‘except with the master’s permission’. This issue is repeated; the author has mentioned it earlier with a better phrasing where he said ‘The marriage of a male slave and a female slave without the master’s permission is suspended’, and here he said ‘not valid’. So it is better to say ‘not executed’ or that the lack of validity in transactions which include marriage means lack of execution, such that what was mentioned in its chapter as a digression is not counted as repetition of what was said before, or the meaning is that it is valid but not executed like the contract of a mediator. Malik said: A male slave may marry without his master’s permission because he owns divorce so he owns marriage. Our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): ‘Any male slave who marries without his master’s permission is a fornicator’ – meaning an adulterer.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It opens the chapter on the marriage of slaves, defining the term ‘raqiq’ and explaining its connection to the free persons section. The core ruling is stated: the marriage of a slave (male or female), a mukatab, a mudabbar, or an umm walad is not valid without the master’s permission. The author addresses a seeming repetition from earlier where the ruling was ‘suspended’; here it is ‘not valid’. The commentator resolves this by clarifying that ‘not valid’ means ‘not executed’ (like a mediator’s contract). Then the passage presents a dispute with Imam Malik, who argues that a slave can marry without permission because he owns divorce. The Hanafi response is the hadith: ‘Any male slave who marries without his master’s permission is a fornicator.’ This hadith is a clear proof from the Sunnah, making the prohibition definitive. The word ‘cahir’ (fornicator) indicates the marriage is invalid and sinful. Thus, the Hanafi position is that permission is a condition for validity.

Key Terms
الرقيق (al-raqiq): The male slave or owned person, used for both singular and plural, derived from riqq (weakness).
عاهر (cahir): A fornicator; here used to indicate the invalidity of the marriage and the sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A sinner but marriage valid.
B) A fornicator (cahir).
C) A rebel.
D) A slave exercising his right.

Key Takeaway
A slave's marriage without master's permission is invalid and akin to fornication; permission is a necessary condition for validity.

Master’s Command to Divorce: Implied Approval of Slave’s Marriage
Ruling on master's divorce command as approval

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes between a command for revocable divorce and other divorce commands regarding approval of a suspended marriage, and apply the ruling to similar guardian-consent scenarios.

Core Idea
Only a command for revocable divorce implies approval of a suspended marriage; other divorce commands imply rejection

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq examines a nuanced scenario: a slave marries without his master's permission, creating a suspended marriage contract. The master may later utter a command to divorce. But does any divorce command constitute implicit approval? The Hanafi school, as explained here, carefully distinguishes between revocable and irrevocable divorce commands, deriving a rule that only the former logically presupposes a valid marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled on and its legal outcome. The act is the master's command to his slave to divorce. The ruling is whether that command constitutes implicit approval of the slave's previously unauthorized marriage.
The specific phrase used by the master determines the ruling.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof the text relies on. Here the proof is logical: a revocable divorce (الرجعي) can only occur after a valid marriage, so commanding it presumes the marriage's validity.
This is an example of استدلال عقلي (rational inference) from the nature of revocable divorce.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the proof leads to the ruling. The command 'طلقها رجعية' entails that the master treats the marriage as valid, thereby approving it. In contrast, 'طلقها' or 'فارقها' could imply rejection, especially given the slave's rebelliousness.
The key is that 'رجعية' is a legal term that presupposes a valid marriage.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the differing view. Ibn Abi Layla held that even 'طلقها' alone constitutes approval, drawing an analogy to a third-party marriage where the groom's 'طلقها' is approval.
The disagreement centers on whether the master is analogous to a third-party agent.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school rejects Ibn Abi Layla's analogy because the master does not have the power to divorce his slave's wife directly, whereas a third-party marriage agent is like an assistant. Hence only the revocable command is approval.
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطلقها رجعيّة إجازة للنكاح الموقوف، لا طلقها أو فارقها. أي قول المولى لعبده الذي تزوج بغير إذنه: طلقها طلقة رجعية إجازة للنكاح لأن الرجعي لا يكون إلا بعد النكاح الصحيح، فكان الأمر بالطلاق الرجعي إجازة اقتضاء، والمراد بالنكاح النكاح المعهود ولو فاسدا وهو نكاح العبد بغير إذن السيد، وقوله: "الموقوف" يستفاد منه أن عقده عقد فضولي، فتجري فيه الأحكام من فسخ العبد والمرأة له قبل إجازة المولى. لا طلقها: أي لا يكون إجازة للنكاح قول المولى لعبده الذي تزوج بغير إذنه. لا طلقها أو فارقها أي لو تزوج عبد بغير إذن المولى، فقال له المولى بعد ما بلغه خبر النكاح: طلقها من غير قيد الرجعة أو قال: فارقها لم يكن هذا إجازة للنكاح؛ لأنه يحتمل الرد أي رد العقد ومتاركته، سمي طلاقا ومفارقة وهو أليق بحال العبد المتمرّد ؛ لأن دليل الفساد قائم وهو التمرد، ومحمل كلام المولى عليه، وقال ابن أبي ليلى: "طلقها" إجازة أيضاً، ولو زوج فضولي رجلاً امرأة فقال الرجل: "طلقها" يكون إجازة؛ لأن فعل الفضولي إعانة كالوكيل، والإعانة تنهض سببا لإمضاء تصرفه بخلاف المولى فإنه لا يملك التطليق بإجازته طلاق عبده لاستقلال العبد به.
And if he says 'Divorce her with a revocable divorce,' it is an approval of the suspended marriage. Not if he says 'Divorce her' or 'Separate from her.' That is: The master's saying to his slave who married without his permission: 'Divorce her with a revocable divorce' is an approval of the marriage because the revocable divorce only occurs after a valid marriage, so the command of revocable divorce is an implied approval. The intended meaning of marriage is the usual marriage, even if defective, which is the slave's marriage without the master's permission. His saying 'the suspended' indicates that his contract is a contract of a third party, so the rules of rescission by the slave and the woman before the master's approval apply. 'Not if he says: Divorce her' means: that the master's saying to his slave who married without his permission is not an approval. 'Not if he says: Divorce her or separate from her' means: If a slave marries without the master's permission, and the master, after hearing of the marriage, says: 'Divorce her' without specifying revocability, or says: 'Separate from her,' this is not an approval of the marriage because it may imply rejection, i.e., rejection of the contract and leaving it. It is called 'divorce' and 'separation,' and it is more appropriate for the rebellious slave because the evidence of invalidity exists—his rebelliousness—and the master's words are interpreted accordingly. Ibn Abi Layla said: 'Divorce her' is also an approval. And if a third party marries a man to a woman and the man says: 'Divorce her,' it is an approval, because the third party's action is assistance like an agent, and assistance becomes a cause for executing his action, unlike the master, who does not have the power to effect a divorce through his approval because the slave is independent in that.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal effect of a master's command to his slave who married without permission. The key distinction is between saying 'طلقها رجعية' (divorce her with a revocable divorce) and 'طلقها بائنا' or 'فارقها' (divorce her irrevocably or leave her). The first constitutes an implicit approval (إجازة اقتضاء) of the marriage, because a revocable divorce presupposes a valid marriage. The second does not, because the words are ambiguous and could mean rejection. The commentary explains that the marriage is suspended (موقوف) like a contract made by a third party (فضولي), and the slave or woman can rescind before approval. Ibn Abi Layla differed, considering 'طلقها' alone as approval. The passage also compares with a third-party marriage (فضولي) where the husband's 'طلقها' is approval because the third party is akin to an agent.

Key Terms
إجازة اقتضاء (ijāzat iqtiḍā'): Implicit approval inferred from an action that logically presupposes the validity of the preceding act.
نكاح موقوف (nikāḥ mawqūf): A marriage contract pending approval of the guardian (the master), similar to a contract made by a third party (فضولي).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following master's commands to a slave who married without permission constitutes implicit approval of the marriage?
A) 'طلقها' (divorce her)
B) 'فارقها' (separate from her)
C) 'طلقها رجعية' (divorce her with a revocable divorce)
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a master's command for a revocable divorce (only) constitutes implicit approval of the slave's unauthorized marriage.
